Sparse recovery, also known as compressed sensing, is the study of under-determined systems of equations subject to a sparsity constraint. Suppose we know that an unknown vector xвҲҲв„қnрқ‘Ҙsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣx\in\mathbb{R}^{n} has at most rвүӘnmuch-less-thanрқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣr\ll n non-zero entries. We would like to use a measurement matrix MвҲҲв„қkГ—nрқ‘Җsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣM\in\mathbb{R}^{k\times n} to recover the vector xрқ‘Ҙx given measurements y=MвҖӢxрқ‘Ұрқ‘Җрқ‘Ҙy=Mx. The number kрқ‘ҳk of measurements is an important parameter we would like to optimize as it models the equipment cost in physical settings and running times in computational settings. Ideally one would like for the number kрқ‘ҳk of measurements to scale proportionally to the sparsity of the unknown vector xрқ‘Ҙx.

One way of modeling sparse recovery is as вҖңstable sparse recoveryвҖқ. Here we want a distribution в„ів„і\mathcal{M} over kГ—nрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣk\times n matrices such that for any xвҲҲв„қnрқ‘Ҙsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣx\in\mathbb{R}^{n}, with probability вүҘ1вҲ’Оҙabsent1рқӣҝ\geq 1-\delta over рқ‘ҙвҲјв„іsimilar-toрқ‘ҙв„і\boldsymbol{M}\sim\mathcal{M}, we can construct a vector x^^рқ‘Ҙ\hat{x} from рқ‘ҙвҖӢxрқ‘ҙрқ‘Ҙ\boldsymbol{M}x such thatвҖ–xвҲ’x^вҖ–pвүӨ(1+Оө)вҖӢminrвҖӢ-sparseвҖӢxвҖІвҒЎвҖ–xвҲ’xвҖІвҖ–p.subscriptnormрқ‘Ҙ^рқ‘Ҙрқ‘қ1рқңҖsubscriptрқ‘ҹ-sparsesuperscriptрқ‘ҘвҖІsubscriptnormрқ‘Ҙsuperscriptрқ‘ҘвҖІрқ‘қ\displaystyle\|{x-\hat{x}}\|_{p}\leq(1+\varepsilon)\min_{r\text{-sparse}\,x^{\prime}}\|x-x^{\prime}\|_{p}.Note that the above formulation is more robust as it does not require the underlying vector xрқ‘Ҙx to be exactly rрқ‘ҹr-sparse and instead asks to recover the top rрқ‘ҹr coordinates of xрқ‘Ҙx.

For p=2рқ‘қ2p=2, it is known that k=ОҳвҖӢ(ОөвҲ’1вҖӢrвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n/r))рқ‘ҳОҳsuperscriptрқңҖ1рқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹk=\Theta(\varepsilon^{-1}r\log(n/r)) measurements is both necessary and sufficient [6, 9, 22, 4]. See [23] and references therein for upper and lower bounds for other values of pрқ‘қp.

In the same vein, the problem of low rank matrix recovery has been studied. See [5, 35] and references therein for earlier work and numerous applications. In this problem, the aim is to recover a low rank matrix AрқҗҙA using linear measurements. Here we want a distribution в„ів„і\mathcal{M} over linear operators M:в„қnГ—nвҶ’в„қk:рқ‘ҖвҶ’superscriptв„қрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ҳM:\mathbb{R}^{n\times n}\rightarrow\mathbb{R}^{k}, such that for any low rank matrix AрқҗҙA, with probability вүҘ1вҲ’Оҙabsent1рқӣҝ\geq 1-\delta over рқ‘ҙвҲјв„іsimilar-toрқ‘ҙв„і\boldsymbol{M}\sim\mathcal{M}, we can construct a matrix A^^рқҗҙ\hat{A} from в„івҖӢ(A)в„ірқҗҙ\mathcal{M}(A) such that the reconstruction error вҖ–AвҲ’A^вҖ–рқ–Ҙ2superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙ^рқҗҙрқ–Ҙ2\|A-\hat{A}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2} is small. Note that a linear operator M:в„қnГ—nвҶ’в„қk:рқ‘ҖвҶ’superscriptв„қрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ҳM:\mathbb{R}^{n\times n}\rightarrow\mathbb{R}^{k} can be equivalently represented as a matrix MвҲҲв„қkГ—n2рқ‘Җsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2M\in\mathbb{R}^{k\times n^{2}} such that MвӢ…vecвҖӢ(A)=MвҖӢ(A)вӢ…рқ‘Җvecрқҗҙрқ‘ҖрқҗҙM\cdot\text{vec}(A)=M(A) where vecвҖӢ(A)vecрқҗҙ\text{vec}(A) denotes the appropriate flattening of the matrix AрқҗҙA into a vector. We call the rows of Mрқ‘ҖM linear measurements. Without loss of generality, we can assume that the rows of the matrix Mрқ‘ҖM are orthonormal, as the responses for non-orthonormal queries can be obtained via a simple change of basis.

In addition, to model the measurement error that occurs in practice, it is a standard assumption that when querying with Mрқ‘ҖM, we receive MвӢ…vecвҒЎ(A)+рқ’ҲвӢ…рқ‘Җvecрқҗҙрқ’ҲM\cdot\operatorname{vec}(A)+\boldsymbol{g}, where рқ’Ҳрқ’Ҳ\boldsymbol{g} is a kрқ‘ҳk-dimensional vector with independent Gaussian random variables of mean 00 and variance Пғ2superscriptрқңҺ2\sigma^{2}, and we hope to reconstruct AрқҗҙA with small error from MвӢ…vecвҒЎ(A)+рқ’ҲвӢ…рқ‘Җvecрқҗҙрқ’ҲM\cdot\operatorname{vec}(A)+\boldsymbol{g}. Clearly, when AрқҗҙA has rank rрқ‘ҹr, we need to perform О©вҖӢ(nвҖӢr)О©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹ\Omega(nr) linear measurements, as the matrix AрқҗҙA has ОҳвҖӢ(nвҖӢr)Оҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹ\Theta(nr) independent parameters. Hence, the aim is to perform not many more linear measurements than nвҖӢrрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹnr while being able to obtain an estimate A^^рқҗҙ\hat{A} for AрқҗҙA with low estimation error.

Given a rank-rрқ‘ҹr matrix AрқҗҙA, [5] show that if the kГ—n2рқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2k\times n^{2} matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} is constructed with independent standard Gaussian entries, then with probability вүҘ1вҲ’expвҒЎ(вҲ’cвҖӢn)absent1рқ‘җрқ‘ӣ\geq 1-\exp(-cn), an estimate A^^рқҗҙ\hat{A} can be constructed from рқ‘ҙвӢ…vecвҒЎ(A)+рқ’ҲвӢ…рқ‘ҙvecрқҗҙрқ’Ҳ\boldsymbol{M}\cdot\operatorname{vec}(A)+\boldsymbol{g} such thatвҖ–AвҲ’A^вҖ–рқ–Ҙ2вүӨOвҖӢ(nвҖӢrвҖӢПғ2/k).superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙ^рқҗҙрқ–Ҙ2рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹsuperscriptрқңҺ2рқ‘ҳ\|A-\hat{A}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}\leq O(nr\sigma^{2}/k). They use the restricted isometry property (RIP) of the Gaussian matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} to obtain algorithms that give an estimate A^^рқҗҙ\hat{A}. The error bound is intuitive since the reconstruction error increases with increasing noise and proportionally goes down when the number of measurements kрқ‘ҳk increases.

While we formulated the sparse recovery and matrix recovery problems in a non-adaptive way, there have been works which study adaptive algorithms for sparse recovery. Here we can produce matrices рқ‘ҙ(i)superscriptрқ‘ҙрқ‘–\boldsymbol{M}^{(i)} adaptively based on the responses received рқ‘ҙ(1)вҖӢx,рқ‘ҙ(2)вҖӢx,вҖҰ,рқ‘ҙ(iвҲ’1)вҖӢxsuperscriptрқ‘ҙ1рқ‘Ҙsuperscriptрқ‘ҙ2рқ‘ҘвҖҰsuperscriptрқ‘ҙрқ‘–1рқ‘Ҙ\boldsymbol{M}^{(1)}x,\boldsymbol{M}^{(2)}x,\ldots,\boldsymbol{M}^{(i-1)}x and the hope is that allowing for adaptive algorithms with a small number of adaptive rounds, we obtain algorithms that overall perform fewer linear measurements than non-adaptive algorithms with the same reconstruction error. It is additionally assumed that the noise across different rounds is independent. For sparse recovery, in the case of p=2рқ‘қ2p=2, it is known that over OвҖӢ(logвҒЎlogвҒЎn)рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣO(\log\log n) rounds adaptivity, a total of OвҖӢ(ОөвҲ’1вҖӢrвҖӢlogвҒЎlogвҒЎ(nвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n/r)))рқ‘ӮsuperscriptрқңҖ1рқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹO(\varepsilon^{-1}r\log\log(n\log(n/r))) linear measurements suffices [14, 21], improving over the requirement of ОҳвҖӢ(ОөвҲ’1вҖӢrвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n/r))ОҳsuperscriptрқңҖ1рқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹ\Theta(\varepsilon^{-1}r\log(n/r)) linear measurements for non-adaptive algorithms. For a constant ОөрқңҖ\varepsilon, for any number of rounds, it is known that О©вҖӢ(r+logвҒЎlogвҒЎn)О©рқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣ\Omega(r+\log\log n) linear measurements are required [23]. Recently, [16] gave a lower bound on the total number of measurements if the number of adaptive rounds is constant.

While there has been a lot of interest in adaptive sparse recovery, both from the algorithms and the lower bounds perspective, the adaptive matrix recovery problem surprisingly does not seem to have any lower bounds. In adaptive matrix recovery, similar to adaptive sparse recovery, one is allowed to query a matrix M(i)superscriptрқ‘Җрқ‘–M^{(i)} in round iрқ‘–i based on the responses received in the previous rounds, and again the hope is that with more rounds of adaptivity, the total number of linear measurements that is to be performed decreases. There is some work that studies adaptive matrix recovery with 222 rounds of adaptivity (see [34] and references therein) but the full landscape of adaptive algorithms for matrix recovery seems unexplored.

We address this from the lower bounds side in this work. We show lower bounds on adaptive algorithms that recover a rank-rрқ‘ҹr matrix of the form (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}, where the coordinates of рқ’–isubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–\boldsymbol{u}_{i} and рқ’—isubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–\boldsymbol{v}_{i} are sampled independently from the standard Gaussian distribution. Without loss of generality111In general, in the sparse recovery and matrix recovery models, the algorithms may make the same query and obtain responses with independent noise added which can be used to say obtain more accurate result using the median/mean estimator. But all the algorithms we are aware of for sparse recovery and matrix recovery do not explore independence of noise across queries in this way., we assume that the measurement matrix M(i)superscriptрқ‘Җрқ‘–M^{(i)} in each round iрқ‘–i has orthonormal rows. We also assume that for iвү jрқ‘–рқ‘—i\neq j, the measurement matrices M(i)вҖӢ(M(j))рқ–і=0superscriptрқ‘Җрқ‘–superscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Җрқ‘—рқ–і0M^{(i)}(M^{(j)})^{\mathsf{T}}=0, i.e., measurements across adaptive rounds are orthonormal, since non-orthonormal measurements can be reconstructed from orthonormal measurement matrices by a change of basis.

We now give an alternate way of looking at the adaptive sparse recovery problem: Fix a set of vectors u1,вҖҰ,ursubscriptрқ‘ў1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘ҹu_{1},\ldots,u_{r} and v1,вҖҰ,vrsubscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘ҹv_{1},\ldots,v_{r} and let the underlying matrix we want to reconstruct be (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} for a large enough constant Оұрқӣј\alpha. In round 111, we query a matrix рқ‘ҙ(1)вҲҲв„қkГ—n2superscriptрқ‘ҙ1superscriptв„қрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2\boldsymbol{M}^{(1)}\in\mathbb{R}^{k\times n^{2}} drawn from an appropriate distribution and receive the response vector рқ’“(1)=рқ‘ҙ(1)вҖӢvecвҒЎ((Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–і)+рқ’Ҳ(1)superscriptрқ’“1superscriptрқ‘ҙ1vecрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–іsuperscriptрқ’Ҳ1\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}=\boldsymbol{M}^{(1)}\operatorname{vec}((\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}})+\boldsymbol{g}^{(1)} where рқ’Ҳ(1)superscriptрқ’Ҳ1\boldsymbol{g}^{(1)} is a vector of independent Gaussian random variables with mean 00 and variance Пғ2superscriptрқңҺ2\sigma^{2}. In round 222, as a function of рқ‘ҙ(1)superscriptрқ‘ҙ1\boldsymbol{M}^{(1)} and рқ’“(1)superscriptрқ’“1\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)} and our randomness, we query a random matrix рқ‘ҙ(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҲҲв„қkГ—n2superscriptрқ‘ҙ2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1superscriptв„қрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2\boldsymbol{M}^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}]\in\mathbb{R}^{k\times n^{2}} and receive a response vectorрқ’“(2)=(рқ‘ҙ(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)])вҖӢvecвҒЎ((Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1рқ’“uiвҖӢviрқ–і)+рқ’Ҳ(2)superscriptрқ’“2superscriptрқ‘ҙ2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1vecрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ’“subscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–іsuperscriptрқ’Ҳ2\boldsymbol{r}^{(2)}=(\boldsymbol{M}^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}])\operatorname{vec}((\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{\boldsymbol{r}}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}})+\boldsymbol{g}^{(2)}where рқ’Ҳ(2)superscriptрқ’Ҳ2\boldsymbol{g}^{(2)} is again a vector with independent Gaussian entries and independent of рқ’Ҳ(1)superscriptрқ’Ҳ1\boldsymbol{g}^{(1)}, and so on. Crucially, using the rotational invariance of Gaussian random vectors, if рқ‘®рқ‘®\boldsymbol{G} is an nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n matrix with independent Gaussian random variables with mean 00 and variance Пғ2superscriptрқңҺ2\sigma^{2}, the response рқ’“(1)superscriptрқ’“1\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)} has the same distribution as(рқ‘ҙ(1))вӢ…vecвҒЎ((Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–і+рқ‘®)вӢ…superscriptрқ‘ҙ1vecрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–ірқ‘®(\boldsymbol{M}^{(1)})\cdot\operatorname{vec}((\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}+\boldsymbol{G})and as рқ‘ҙ(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]superscriptрқ‘ҙ2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1\boldsymbol{M}^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}] is chosen to be orthonormal to рқ‘ҙ(1)superscriptрқ‘ҙ1\boldsymbol{M}^{(1)}, the distribution of рқ’“(2)superscriptрқ’“2\boldsymbol{r}^{(2)} conditioned on рқ’“(1)superscriptрқ’“1\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)} is the same as that of(рқ‘ҙ(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)])вӢ…(vecвҒЎ((Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–і+рқ‘®)).вӢ…superscriptрқ‘ҙ2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1vecрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–ірқ‘®(\boldsymbol{M}^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}])\cdot(\operatorname{vec}((\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}+\boldsymbol{G})).

Thus, any adaptive matrix recovery algorithm can be seen as performing non-noisy adaptive measurements on the matrix (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–і+рқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–ірқ‘®(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}+\boldsymbol{G} where the Gaussian matrix рқ‘®рқ‘®\boldsymbol{G} is sampled independently of the measurement algorithm. From the responses the algorithm receives, it then tries to reconstruct the matrix (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}. This way of looking at adaptive sparse recovery immediately yields an adaptive algorithm: when the smallest singular value of (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} is a constant times larger than вҖ–рқ‘®вҖ–2subscriptnormрқ‘®2\|\boldsymbol{G}\|_{2}, then the power method with a block size of rрқ‘ҹr outputs an approximation of (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} in OвҖӢ(logвҒЎn)рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣO(\log n) rounds. Note that rрқ‘ҹr matrix-vector products can be implemented using nвҖӢrрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹnr linear measurements. More generally, Gu [12] showed that using power iteration with a block size of k/nрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣk/n (for kвүҘnвҖӢrрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹk\geq nr), we can obtain an approximation in OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n2/k))рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳO(\log(n^{2}/k)) adaptive rounds. Thusthe already existing algorithms exhibit a no. of measurements vs no. of rounds trade-off.

From results in random matrix theory, we have that вҖ–рқ‘®вҖ–2вүҲПғвҖӢnsubscriptnormрқ‘®2рқңҺрқ‘ӣ\|\boldsymbol{G}\|_{2}\approx\sigma\sqrt{n} with high probability. And as we are interested in reconstruction when the vectors u1,вҖҰ,ursubscriptрқ‘ў1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘ҹu_{1},\ldots,u_{r} and v1,вҖҰ,vrsubscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘ҹv_{1},\ldots,v_{r} follow the Gaussian distribution we also have that вҖ–uiвҖ–2вүҲвҖ–viвҖ–2вүҲnsubscriptnormsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–2subscriptnormsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–2рқ‘ӣ\|u_{i}\|_{2}\approx\|v_{i}\|_{2}\approx\sqrt{n} simultaneously with large probability. Thus, to make the extraction of (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} information-theoretically possible, we need to assume that ОұвүіПғgreater-than-or-equivalent-toрқӣјрқңҺ\alpha\gtrsim\sigma. Hence, in this work we assume that Пғ=1рқңҺ1\sigma=1 and that Оұрқӣј\alpha is a large enough constant, and we study lower bounds on adaptive matrix recovery algorithms.

If the vectors u1,вҖҰ,ursubscriptрқ‘ў1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘ҹu_{1},\ldots,u_{r} and v1,вҖҰ,vrsubscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘ҹv_{1},\ldots,v_{r} are sampled from the standard nрқ‘ӣn dimensional Gaussian distribution and rвүӨn/2рқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣ2r\leq n/2, we also have that with high probabilityвҖ–(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–івҖ–рқ–Ҙ2вүҲОұ2вҖӢnвҖӢr.superscriptsubscriptnormрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–ірқ–Ҙ2superscriptрқӣј2рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹ\|(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}\approx\alpha^{2}nr.Now the algorithms of [5], which use a uniform random Gaussian matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} with mрқ‘ҡm rows as the measurement matrix, for (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1uiвҖӢviрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘–1subscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} reconstruct a matrix A^^рқҗҙ\hat{A} such thatвҖ–A^вҲ’(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–івҖ–рқ–Ҙ2вүӨCвҖӢnвҖӢrвҖӢПғm2msuperscriptsubscriptnorm^рқҗҙрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–ірқ–Ҙ2рқҗ¶рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҡ2рқ‘ҡ\|\hat{A}-(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}\leq C\frac{nr\sigma_{m}^{2}}{m} where ПғmsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҡ\sigma_{m} is the measurement error.As we assumed above that Пғ=1рқңҺ1\sigma=1 when measuring with a matrix with orthonormal rows, we assume that the measurement error ПғmsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҡ\sigma_{m} when measuring with a Gaussian matrix is nрқ‘ӣn, as each row of рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} has n2superscriptрқ‘ӣ2n^{2} independent Gaussian coordinates and therefore has a norm вүҲnabsentрқ‘ӣ\approx n. Thus, using reconstruction algorithms from [5], we obtain a matrix A^^рқҗҙ\hat{A} satisfyingвҖ–A^вҲ’(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–івҖ–рқ–Ҙ2вүӨCвҖӢn3вҖӢrm.superscriptsubscriptnorm^рқҗҙрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–ірқ–Ҙ2рқҗ¶superscriptрқ‘ӣ3рқ‘ҹрқ‘ҡ\|\hat{A}-(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}\leq C\frac{n^{3}r}{m}.Now, to make вҖ–A^вҲ’(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–івҖ–рқ–Ҙ2вүӨ(1/10)вҖӢвҖ–(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–івҖ–рқ–Ҙ2superscriptsubscriptnorm^рқҗҙрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–ірқ–Ҙ2110superscriptsubscriptnormрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–ірқ–Ҙ2\|\hat{A}-(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}\leq(1/10)\|(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}, we need to set m=ОҳвҖӢ(n2/Оұ2)рқ‘ҡОҳsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2superscriptрқӣј2m=\Theta(n^{2}/\alpha^{2}). Hence, in the parameter regimes we study, the algorithms of [5] need to perform О©вҖӢ(n2)О©superscriptрқ‘ӣ2\Omega(n^{2}) non-adaptive queries, which essentially means that they have to read a constant fraction of the n2superscriptрқ‘ӣ2n^{2} entries in the matrix. While the power method performs OвҖӢ(nвҖӢr)рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹO(nr) linear measurements in each round over OвҖӢ(logвҒЎn)рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣO(\log n) adaptive rounds to output an approximation A^^рқҗҙ\hat{A}. The question we ask is:вҖңIs the power method optimal? Are there algorithms that have oвҖӢ(logвҒЎn)рқ‘ңрқ‘ӣo(\log n) adaptive rounds and use n2вҲ’ОІsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқӣҪn^{2-\beta} measurements in each round?вҖқWe answer this question by showing that any algorithm that has oвҖӢ(logвҒЎn/logвҒЎlogвҒЎn)рқ‘ңрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣo(\log n/\log\log n) adaptive rounds must use вүҘn2вҲ’ОІabsentsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқӣҪ\geq n^{2-\beta} linear measurements, for any constant ОІ>0рқӣҪ0\beta>0, in each round. The lower bound shows that power method is essentially optimal if we want to use n2вҲ’ОІsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқӣҪn^{2-\beta} linear measurements in each round and that any algorithm with oвҖӢ(logвҒЎn/logвҒЎlogвҒЎn)рқ‘ңрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣo(\log n/\log\log n) adaptive rounds essentially reads the whole matrix.

We further obtain a rounds vs measurements trade-off for many numerical linear algebra problems in the sensing model. In this model, there is an nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n matrix AрқҗҙA with which we can interact only using general linear measurements and we want to solve problems such as spectral norm low rank approximation of AрқҗҙA, Frobenius norm low rank approximation of AрқҗҙA, etc. In general, numerical linear algebra algorithms assume that they either have access to the entire matrix or that the matrix is accessible in the matrix-vector product model where one can query a vector vрқ‘Јv and obtain the result AвӢ…vвӢ…рқҗҙрқ‘ЈA\cdot v. Recently, the vector-matrix-vector product model has received significant attention as well. Linear measurements are more powerful than both the matrix-vector product model and the vector-matrix-vector product model. Any matrix vector product AвӢ…vвӢ…рқҗҙрқ‘ЈA\cdot v can be computed using nрқ‘ӣn linear measurements of AрқҗҙA and any vector-matrix-vector product uрқ–івҖӢAвҖӢvsuperscriptрқ‘ўрқ–ірқҗҙрқ‘Јu^{\mathsf{T}}Av can be computed using a single linear measurement of AрқҗҙA. Thus, the model of general linear measurements may lead to faster algorithms.

For certain problems in numerical linear algebra, general linear measurements are significantly more powerful than the matrix-vector product model. Indeed, for computing the trace of an nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n matrix AрқҗҙA, one can do this exactly with a single deterministic general linear measurement, just by adding up the diagonal entries of AрқҗҙA. However, in the matrix-vector product model, it is known that О©вҖӢ(n)О©рқ‘ӣ\Omega(n) matrix-vector products are needed to compute the trace exactly [29], even if one uses randomization. A number of problems were studied in the vector-matrix-vector product model in [24], and in [32] it was shown that to approximate the trace of AрқҗҙA up to a (1+Оө)1рқңҖ(1+\varepsilon)-factor with probability 1вҲ’Оҙ1рқӣҝ1-\delta, one needs О©вҖӢ(ОөвҲ’2вҖӢlogвҒЎ(1/Оҙ))О©superscriptрқңҖ21рқӣҝ\Omega(\varepsilon^{-2}\log(1/\delta)) queries. This contrasts sharply with the single deterministic general linear measurement for computing the trace exactly. Thus, there are good reasons to conjecture that general linear measurements may lead to algorithms requiring fewer rounds of adaptivity compared to algorithms in the matrix-vector product query model. Surprisingly, our lower bounds show that for many numerical linear algebra problems, linear measurements do not give much advantage over matrix-vector products.

We assume that there is an unknown rank-rрқ‘ҹr matrix AвҲҲв„қnГ—nрқҗҙsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣA\in\mathbb{R}^{n\times n} to be recovered. Given any linear measurement qвҲҲв„қn2рқ‘һsuperscriptв„қsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2q\in\mathbb{R}^{n^{2}}, we receive a response вҹЁq,vecвҒЎ(A)вҹ©+рқ’Ҳрқ‘һvecрқҗҙрқ’Ҳ\langle q,\operatorname{vec}(A)\rangle+\boldsymbol{g}, where рқ’ҲвҲјNвҖӢ(0,вҖ–qвҖ–22)similar-toрқ’Ҳрқ‘Ғ0superscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘һ22\boldsymbol{g}\sim N(0,\|q\|_{2}^{2}). We further assume that the noise for two different measurements is independent. Without loss of generality, we also assume throughout that all the queries an algorithm makes across all rounds form a matrix with orthonormal rows. Our main result for adaptive matrix sensing is as follows:

In our results, we assumed that given a linear measurement qвҲҲв„қn2рқ‘һsuperscriptв„қsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2q\in\mathbb{R}^{n^{2}}, the response is distributed as NвҖӢ(вҹЁq,vecвҒЎ(A)вҹ©,вҖ–qвҖ–22)рқ‘Ғрқ‘һvecрқҗҙsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘һ22N(\langle q,\operatorname{vec}(A)\rangle,\|q\|_{2}^{2}). Our lower bounds also hold when the response is distributed as NвҖӢ(вҹЁq,vecвҒЎ(A)вҹ©,Пғ2вҖӢвҖ–qвҖ–22)рқ‘Ғрқ‘һvecрқҗҙsuperscriptрқңҺ2superscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘һ22N(\langle q,\operatorname{vec}(A)\rangle,\sigma^{2}\|q\|_{2}^{2}) for any parameter ПғрқңҺ\sigma such that cвҖІвүӨПғвүӨ1superscriptрқ‘җвҖІрқңҺ1c^{\prime}\leq\sigma\leq 1, where cвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘җвҖІc^{\prime} is a constant. This can be seen by simply scaling the matrix AрқҗҙA in the theorem above and adjusting the constants while proving the theorem.

The problem of tensor recovery with linear measurements has also been studied (see [25, 11] and references therein) where given a low rank tensor, the task is to recover an approximation to the tensor with few linear measurements. Our techniques can also be used to obtain lower bounds on adaptive algorithms for tensor recovery. Our main tool, LemmaВ 3.1, readily extends to tensors of higher orders by using the corresponding tail bounds from [31].

We also derive lower bounds for many numerical linear algebra problems in the linear measurements model. Table 1 shows our lower bounds on the number of adaptive rounds required for any randomized algorithm using kрқ‘ҳk general linear measurements in each round. See SectionВ 5 for precise statements and proofs.

Throughout the paper, we use uppercase letters such as G,M,Qрқҗәрқ‘Җрқ‘„G,M,Q to denote matrices and lowercase letters such as u,vрқ‘ўрқ‘Јu,v to denote vectors. For vectors u,vвҲҲв„қnрқ‘ўрқ‘Јsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣu,v\in\mathbb{R}^{n}, uвҠ—vвҲҲв„қn2tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Јsuperscriptв„қsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2u\otimes v\in\mathbb{R}^{n^{2}} denotes the tensor product of uрқ‘ўu and vрқ‘Јv. For an arbitrary matrix MвҲҲв„қmГ—nрқ‘Җsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ҡрқ‘ӣM\in\mathbb{R}^{m\times n}, the vector vecвҒЎ(M)вҲҲв„қmвҖӢnvecрқ‘Җsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ҡрқ‘ӣ\operatorname{vec}(M)\in\mathbb{R}^{mn} denotes a flattening of the matrix Mрқ‘ҖM with the convention that vecвҒЎ(uвҖӢvрқ–і)=uвҠ—vvecрқ‘ўsuperscriptрқ‘Јрқ–іtensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј\operatorname{vec}(uv^{\mathsf{T}})=u\otimes v. We use boldface symbols such as рқ‘ҙ,рқ‘®,рқ’–,рқ’—рқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқ’–рқ’—\boldsymbol{M},\boldsymbol{G},\boldsymbol{u},\boldsymbol{v} to denote that these objects are explicitly sampled from an appropriate distribution. We use рқ’Ҳksubscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳ\boldsymbol{g}_{k} to denote a multivariate Gaussian in kрқ‘ҳk dimensions where each coordinate is independently sampled from NвҖӢ(0,1)рқ‘Ғ01N(0,1). We also use G(j)superscriptрқҗәрқ‘—G^{(j)} to denote a collection of jрқ‘—j independent multivariate Gaussian random variables of appropriate dimensions.

Using the rotational invariance of the Gaussian distribution, we argued that any adaptive randomized low rank matrix recovery algorithm with access to a hidden matrix (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} using noisy linear measurements can be seen as a randomized algorithm that has access to a random matrix (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–і+рқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–ірқ‘®(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}+\boldsymbol{G} using perfect linear measurements where each coordinate of рқ‘®рқ‘®\boldsymbol{G} is independently sampled from a Gaussian distribution.

Let рқ’ңрқ’ң\mathcal{A} be any algorithm that satisfies the matrix recovery guarantees with, say, a success probability вүҘ9/10absent910\geq 9/10. Let рқ’ңвҖӢ(X,рққҲ,рқңё)рқ’ңрқ‘ӢрққҲрқңё\mathcal{A}(X,\boldsymbol{\sigma},\boldsymbol{\gamma}) be the output of the randomized algorithm рқ’ңрқ’ң\mathcal{A}, where the hidden matrix is Xрқ‘ӢX, the random seed of рқ’ңрқ’ң\mathcal{A} is denoted by рққҲрққҲ\boldsymbol{\sigma}, and рқңёрқңё\boldsymbol{\gamma} denotes the measurement randomness. Thus, for all such Xрқ‘ӢX,Prрқ‘®,рққҲвҒЎ[рқ’ңвҖІвҖӢ(X+рқ‘®,рққҲ)вҖӢis correct]вүҘ9/10.subscriptPrрқ‘®рққҲsuperscriptрқ’ңвҖІрқ‘Ӣрқ‘®рққҲis correct910\displaystyle\Pr_{\boldsymbol{G},\boldsymbol{\sigma}}[\mathcal{A}^{\prime}(X+\boldsymbol{G},\boldsymbol{\sigma})\,\text{is correct}]\geq 9/10.Here рққҲрққҲ\boldsymbol{\sigma} denotes the randomness used by the algorithm рқ’ңвҖІsuperscriptрқ’ңвҖІ\mathcal{A}^{\prime}.Now, if рқ‘ҝрқ‘ҝ\boldsymbol{X} is a random matrix constructed as (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} with рқ’–i,рқ’—isubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–subscriptрқ’—рқ‘–\boldsymbol{u}_{i},\boldsymbol{v}_{i} being random vectors with independent Gaussian entries of mean 00 and variance 111, then with probability вүҘ99/100absent99100\geq 99/100, вҖ–рқ‘ҝвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2=ОҳвҖӢ(nвҖӢr)superscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘ҝрқ–Ҙ2Оҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹ\|\boldsymbol{X}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}=\Theta(nr). Thus,Prрқ‘ҝ,рқ‘®,ПғвҒЎ[рқ’ңвҖІвҖӢ(рқ‘ҝ+рқ‘®,рққҲ)вҖӢis correct]вүҘ8/10.subscriptPrрқ‘ҝрқ‘®рқңҺsuperscriptрқ’ңвҖІрқ‘ҝрқ‘®рққҲis correct810\Pr_{\boldsymbol{X},\boldsymbol{G},\sigma}[\mathcal{A}^{\prime}(\boldsymbol{X}+\boldsymbol{G},\boldsymbol{\sigma})\,\text{is correct}]\geq 8/10.Hence, there exists some fixed ПғрқңҺ\sigma such thatPrрқ‘ҝ,рқ‘®вҒЎ[рқ’ңвҖІвҖӢ(рқ‘ҝ+рқ‘®,Пғ)вҖӢis correct]вүҘ8/10.subscriptPrрқ‘ҝрқ‘®superscriptрқ’ңвҖІрқ‘ҝрқ‘®рқңҺis correct810\displaystyle\Pr_{\boldsymbol{X},\boldsymbol{G}}[\mathcal{A}^{\prime}(\boldsymbol{X}+\boldsymbol{G},\sigma)\,\text{is correct}]\geq 8/10.Thus, the existence of a randomized algorithm that solves low rank matrix recovery as in TheoremВ 1.1 implies the existence of a deterministic algorithm which given access to perfect linear measurements of random matrix (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–і+рқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–ірқ‘®(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}+\boldsymbol{G} outputs a reconstruction of (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} with probability вүҘ8/10absent810\geq 8/10. This is essentially a reduction from randomized algorithms to deterministic algorithms using YaoвҖҷs lemma. From here on, we prove lower bounds on such deterministic algorithms and conclude the lower bounds in TheoremВ 1.1. For simplicity, we explain the proof of our lower bound for r=1рқ‘ҹ1r=1 here and extend to general rрқ‘ҹr later. We consider the random matrix рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} and show how the lower bound proof proceeds.

Note that the matrix рқ‘Ёвү”рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івҲҲв„қnГ—nвү”рқ‘Ёрқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–іsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣ\boldsymbol{A}\coloneqq\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}\in\mathbb{R}^{n\times n} can be flattened to the vector рқ’Ӯ=рқ’Ҳ+(Оұ/n)вҖӢ(рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—)вҲҲв„қn2рқ’Ӯрқ’Ҳрқӣјрқ‘ӣtensor-productрқ’–рқ’—superscriptв„қsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2\boldsymbol{a}=\boldsymbol{g}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})(\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v})\in\mathbb{R}^{n^{2}}. Also, a general linear measurement, which we call a query QвҲҲв„қnГ—nрқ‘„superscriptв„қрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣQ\in\mathbb{R}^{n\times n}, can be vectorized to q=vecвҒЎ(Q)вҲҲв„қn2рқ‘һvecрқ‘„superscriptв„қsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2q=\operatorname{vec}(Q)\in\mathbb{R}^{n^{2}} with QвҖӢ(рқ‘Ё)=вҹЁq,рқ’Ӯвҹ©рқ‘„рқ‘Ёрқ‘һрқ’ӮQ(\boldsymbol{A})=\langle q,\boldsymbol{a}\rangle. Fix any deterministic algorithm. In the first round, the algorithm starts with a fixed matrix Q(1)вҲҲв„қkГ—n2superscriptрқ‘„1superscriptв„қрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2Q^{(1)}\in\mathbb{R}^{k\times n^{2}} that corresponds to the kрқ‘ҳk queries and receives the response рқ’“(1)вү”Q(1)вҖӢрқ’Ӯвү”superscriptрқ’“1superscriptрқ‘„1рқ’Ӯ\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}\coloneqq Q^{(1)}\boldsymbol{a}. Then, as a function of the response рқ’“(1)superscriptрқ’“1\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)} in the first round, the algorithm picks a matrix Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1Q^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}] in the second round and receives the response рқ’“(2)вү”Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вӢ…рқ’Ӯвү”superscriptрқ’“2вӢ…superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1рқ’Ӯ\boldsymbol{r}^{(2)}\coloneqq Q^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}]\cdot\boldsymbol{a}. Similarly, in the iрқ‘–i-th round, the deterministic algorithm picks a matrix Q(i)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1),вҖҰ,рқ’“(iвҲ’1)]вҲҲв„қkГ—n2superscriptрқ‘„рқ‘–superscriptрқ’“1вҖҰsuperscriptрқ’“рқ‘–1superscriptв„қрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2Q^{(i)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)},\ldots,\boldsymbol{r}^{(i-1)}]\in\mathbb{R}^{k\times n^{2}} as a function of рқ’“(1),вҖҰ,рқ’“(iвҲ’1)superscriptрқ’“1вҖҰsuperscriptрқ’“рқ‘–1\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)},\ldots,\boldsymbol{r}^{(i-1)} and receives the response рқ’“(i)вү”Q(i)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1),вҖҰ,рқ’“(iвҲ’1)]вӢ…рқ’Ӯвү”superscriptрқ’“рқ‘–вӢ…superscriptрқ‘„рқ‘–superscriptрқ’“1вҖҰsuperscriptрқ’“рқ‘–1рқ’Ӯ\boldsymbol{r}^{(i)}\coloneqq Q^{(i)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)},\ldots,\boldsymbol{r}^{(i-1)}]\cdot\boldsymbol{a}. Note that we assumed that the query matrices Q(i)superscriptрқ‘„рқ‘–Q^{(i)} chosen by the algorithm have orthonormal rows and also that Q(i)вҖӢ(Q(j))рқ–і=0superscriptрқ‘„рқ‘–superscriptsuperscriptрқ‘„рқ‘—рқ–і0Q^{(i)}(Q^{(j)})^{\mathsf{T}}=0, i.e., the queries across rounds are also orthonormal.

For a fixed u,vвҲҲв„қnрқ‘ўрқ‘Јsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣu,v\in\mathbb{R}^{n}, we see that the response рқ’“(1)=Q(1)вҖӢрқ’Ҳ+(Оұ/n)вҖӢQ(1)вҖӢ(uвҠ—v)superscriptрқ’“1superscriptрқ‘„1рқ’Ҳрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘„1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}=Q^{(1)}\boldsymbol{g}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})Q^{(1)}(u\otimes v). As the matrix Q(1)superscriptрқ‘„1Q^{(1)} has orthonormal rows, the random variable Q(1)вҖӢрқ’ҲвүЎрқ’Ҳksuperscriptрқ‘„1рқ’Ҳsubscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳQ^{(1)}\boldsymbol{g}\equiv\boldsymbol{g}_{k}, where рқ’ҲkвҲјNвҖӢ(0,Ik)similar-tosubscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘Ғ0subscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҳ\boldsymbol{g}_{k}\sim N(0,I_{k}) is drawn from a mean-zero normal distribution with identity covariance. Thus, for fixed u,vрқ‘ўрқ‘Јu,v, the distribution of the first round responses to the algorithm is NвҖӢ((Оұ/n)вҖӢQ(1)вҖӢ(uвҠ—v),Ik)рқ‘Ғрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘„1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Јsubscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҳN((\alpha/\sqrt{n})Q^{(1)}(u\otimes v),I_{k}). Now the key observation is that вҖ–(Оұ/n)вҖӢQ(1)вҖӢ(рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—)вҖ–22=ОҳвҖӢ(Оұ2вҖӢk/n)superscriptsubscriptnormрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘„1tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—22Оҳsuperscriptрқӣј2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\|(\alpha/\sqrt{n})Q^{(1)}(\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v})\|_{2}^{2}=\Theta(\alpha^{2}k/n) with high probability over the inputs (рқ’–,рқ’—)рқ’–рқ’—(\boldsymbol{u},\boldsymbol{v}). This uses a recent concentration result for random tensors due to [31], and critically uses the fact that Q(1)superscriptрқ‘„1Q^{(1)} has operator norm 111 and Frobenius norm kрқ‘ҳ\sqrt{k}. This means that for a large fraction of (u,v)рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј(u,v) pairs, the distribution of the responses seen by the algorithm in the first round is close to NвҖӢ(0,Ik)рқ‘Ғ0subscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҳN(0,I_{k}), and therefore just looking at the response рқ’“(1)superscriptрқ’“1\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}, the algorithm cannot have a lot of вҖңinformationвҖқ about which (u,v)рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј(u,v) pair is involved in the matrix that is unknown to the algorithm. So the query chosen in the second round Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1Q^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}] cannot have a вҖңlargeвҖқ value of Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢ(uвҠ—v)superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘ЈQ^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}](u\otimes v) for most inputs (u,v)рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј(u,v), with a high probability over the Gaussian component of the matrix.

Suppose the value of Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢ(uвҠ—v)superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘ЈQ^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}](u\otimes v) is small. Again, рқ’“(2)=Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢрқ’Ҳ+(Оұ/n)вҖӢQ(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢ(uвҠ—v)superscriptрқ’“2superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1рқ’Ҳрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј\boldsymbol{r}^{(2)}=Q^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}]\boldsymbol{g}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})Q^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}](u\otimes v). Crucially, as the queries in round 222 are orthogonal to the queries in round 111, we have by the rotational invariance of the Gaussian distribution that Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢрқ’Ҳsuperscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1рқ’ҲQ^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}]\boldsymbol{g} is independent of Q(1)вҖӢрқ’Ҳsuperscriptрқ‘„1рқ’ҲQ^{(1)}\boldsymbol{g}, and that Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢрқ’Ҳsuperscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1рқ’ҲQ^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}]\boldsymbol{g} is distributed as NвҖӢ(0,Ik)рқ‘Ғ0subscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҳN(0,I_{k}). So, for a fixed u,vрқ‘ўрқ‘Јu,v, conditioned on the first round response рқ’“(1)superscriptрқ’“1\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}, the distribution of the second round response рқ’“(2)superscriptрқ’“2\boldsymbol{r}^{(2)} is given by NвҖӢ((Оұ/n)вҖӢQ(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢ(uвҠ—v),Ik)вүҲNвҖӢ(0,Ik)рқ‘Ғрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Јsubscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҳрқ‘Ғ0subscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҳN((\alpha/\sqrt{n})Q^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}](u\otimes v),I_{k})\approx N(0,I_{k}) using the assumption that Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢ(uвҠ—v)superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘ЈQ^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}](u\otimes v) is small. We again have that for a large fraction of pairs (u,v)рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј(u,v) for which Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢ(uвҠ—v)superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘ЈQ^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}](u\otimes v) is small, the distribution of the second round response is also close to NвҖӢ(0,Ik)рқ‘Ғ0subscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҳN(0,I_{k}). Therefore, the algorithm again does not gain a lot of information about which (u,v)рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј(u,v) pair is involved in the matrix, and the third round query Q(3)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1),рқ’“(2)]superscriptрқ‘„3superscriptрқ’“1superscriptрқ’“2Q^{(3)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)},\boldsymbol{r}^{(2)}] cannot have a large value of вҖ–Q(3)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1),рқ’“(2)]вҖӢ(uвҠ—v)вҖ–2subscriptnormsuperscriptрқ‘„3superscriptрқ’“1superscriptрқ’“2tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј2\|Q^{(3)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)},\boldsymbol{r}^{(2)}](u\otimes v)\|_{2}. The proof proceeds similarly for further rounds.

To formalize the above intuitive idea, we use Bayes risk lower bounds [7]. We show that with a large probability over the input matrix, the squared projection of рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v} onto the query space of the algorithm is upper bounded and we use an iterative argument to show that an upper bound on the information up until round iрқ‘–i can in turn be used to upper bound the information up until round i+1рқ‘–1i+1. Bayes risk bounds are very general and let us obtain upper bounds on the information learned by a deterministic learner. Concretely, let ОҳОҳ\Theta be a parameter space and рқ’«={PОё:ОёвҲҲОҳ}рқ’«:subscriptрқ‘ғрқңғрқңғОҳ\mathcal{P}=\set{P_{\theta}\,:\theta\in\Theta} be a set of distributions, one for each ОёвҲҲОҳрқңғОҳ\theta\in\Theta. Let wрқ‘Өw be a distribution over ОҳОҳ\Theta. We sample рқңҪвҲјwsimilar-toрқңҪрқ‘Ө\boldsymbol{\theta}\sim w and then рқ’ҷвҲјPрқңҪsimilar-toрқ’ҷsubscriptрқ‘ғрқңҪ\boldsymbol{x}\sim P_{\boldsymbol{\theta}} and provide the learner with рқ’ҷрқ’ҷ\boldsymbol{x}. Given an action space рқ’ңрқ’ң\mathcal{A}, the learner uses a deterministic decision rule рқ”Ў:рқ’івҶ’рқ’ң:рқ”ЎвҶ’рқ’ірқ’ң\mathfrak{d}:\mathcal{X}\rightarrow\mathcal{A} to minimize a 00-111 loss function L:ОҳГ—рқ’ңвҶ’{0,1}:рқҗҝвҶ’Оҳрқ’ң01L:\Theta\times\mathcal{A}\rightarrow\set{0,1} in expectation, i.e.,EрқңҪвҲјwвҒЎ[Eрқ’ҷвҲјPрқңҪвҒЎLвҖӢ(рқңҪ,рқ”ЎвҖӢ(рқ’ҷ))].subscriptEsimilar-toрқңҪрқ‘ӨsubscriptEsimilar-toрқ’ҷsubscriptрқ‘ғрқңҪрқҗҝрқңҪрқ”Ўрқ’ҷ\operatorname{E}_{\boldsymbol{\theta}\sim w}[\operatorname{E}_{\boldsymbol{x}\sim P_{\boldsymbol{\theta}}}L(\boldsymbol{\theta},\mathfrak{d}(\boldsymbol{x}))].Let RBayesвҖӢ(L,Оҳ,w)=infрқ”ЎEрқңҪвҲјwвҖӢ[Eрқ’ҷвҲјPрқңҪвҖӢLвҖӢ(рқңҪ,рқ”ЎвҖӢ(рқ’ҷ))]subscriptрқ‘…BayesрқҗҝОҳрқ‘Өsubscriptinfimumрқ”Ўsubscriptрқҗёsimilar-toрқңҪрқ‘Өdelimited-[]subscriptрқҗёsimilar-toрқ’ҷsubscriptрқ‘ғрқңҪрқҗҝрқңҪрқ”Ўрқ’ҷR_{\textnormal{Bayes}}(L,\Theta,w)=\inf_{\mathfrak{d}}E_{\boldsymbol{\theta}\sim w}[E_{\boldsymbol{x}\sim P_{\boldsymbol{\theta}}}L(\boldsymbol{\theta},\mathfrak{d}(\boldsymbol{x}))] be the loss achievable by the best deterministic decision rule рқ”Ўрқ”Ў\mathfrak{d}. Bayes risk lower bounds let us obtain lower bounds on RBayessubscriptрқ‘…BayesR_{\textnormal{Bayes}}.

In our setting after round 111, we have Оҳ={(u,v):u,vвҲҲв„қn}Оҳ:рқ‘ўрқ‘Јрқ‘ўрқ‘Јsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣ\Theta=\set{(u,v):u,v\in\mathbb{R}^{n}}, wрқ‘Өw is the joint distribution of two independent standard Gaussian random variables in в„қnsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣ\mathbb{R}^{n} and for each (u,v)вҲҲОҳрқ‘ўрқ‘ЈОҳ(u,v)\in\Theta we let PuвҖӢvsubscriptрқ‘ғрқ‘ўрқ‘ЈP_{uv} be the distribution of рқ’“(1)=рқ’Ҳk+(Оұ/n)вҖӢQ(1)вҖӢ(uвҠ—v)superscriptрқ’“1subscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳрқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘„1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}=\boldsymbol{g}_{k}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})Q^{(1)}(u\otimes v), an action space рқ’ңрқ’ң\mathcal{A} of all kГ—n2рқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2k\times n^{2} matrices with orthonormal rows (corresponding to the queries in the next round), and define a 00-111 loss functionLвҖӢ((u,v),Q)={0ifВ вҖӢвҖ–QвҖӢ(uвҠ—v)вҖ–22вүҘT1ifВ вҖӢвҖ–QвҖӢ(uвҠ—v)вҖ–22<Tрқҗҝрқ‘ўрқ‘Јрқ‘„cases0ifВ superscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘„tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј22рқ‘Ү1ifВ superscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘„tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј22рқ‘ҮL((u,v),Q)=\begin{cases}0&\text{if }\|Q(u\otimes v)\|_{2}^{2}\geq T\\1&\text{if }\|Q(u\otimes v)\|_{2}^{2}<T\end{cases}for an appropriate threshold parameter Tрқ‘ҮT. By setting Tрқ‘ҮT appropriately as a function of tрқ‘Ўt, we obtain a Bayes risk lower bound of RBayesвүҘ1вҲ’1/(100вҖӢt2)subscriptрқ‘…Bayes11100superscriptрқ‘Ў2R_{\textnormal{Bayes}}\geq 1-1/(100t^{2}). Thus, we obtain that for any deterministic decision rule рқ”Ўрқ”Ў\mathfrak{d}, with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/10вҖӢtabsent1110рқ‘Ў\geq 1-1/10t over (рқ’–,рқ’—)вҲјwsimilar-toрқ’–рқ’—рқ‘Ө(\boldsymbol{u},\boldsymbol{v})\sim w, we haveEрқ’“(1)вҲјPрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—вҒЎ[LвҖӢ((рқ’–,рқ’—),рқ”ЎвҖӢ(рқ’“(1)))]вүҘ1вҲ’1/10вҖӢtsubscriptEsimilar-tosuperscriptрқ’“1subscriptрқ‘ғрқ’–рқ’—рқҗҝрқ’–рқ’—рқ”Ўsuperscriptрқ’“11110рқ‘Ў\displaystyle\operatorname{E}_{\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}\sim P_{\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}}}[L((\boldsymbol{u},\boldsymbol{v}),\mathfrak{d}(\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}))]\geq 1-1/10tand in particular, we have that with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/10вҖӢtabsent1110рқ‘Ў\geq 1-1/10t over (рқ’–,рқ’—)вҲјwsimilar-toрқ’–рқ’—рқ‘Ө(\boldsymbol{u},\boldsymbol{v})\sim w,Prрқ’“(1)вҲјPрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—вҒЎ[вҖ–Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢ(рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—)вҖ–22<T]вүҘ1вҲ’1/10вҖӢt.subscriptPrsimilar-tosuperscriptрқ’“1subscriptрқ‘ғрқ’–рқ’—superscriptsubscriptnormsuperscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—22рқ‘Ү1110рқ‘Ў\displaystyle\Pr_{\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}\sim P_{\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}}}[\|Q^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}](\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v})\|_{2}^{2}<T]\geq 1-1/10t.(2)The above statement essentially says that with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/10вҖӢtabsent1110рқ‘Ў\geq 1-1/10t over the inputs (рқ’–,рқ’—)рқ’–рқ’—(\boldsymbol{u},\boldsymbol{v}), the second query Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1Q^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}] chosen by the deterministic algorithm has the property that вҖ–Q(2)вҖӢ[рқ’“(1)]вҖӢ(рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—)вҖ–22<Tsuperscriptsubscriptnormsuperscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ’“1tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—22рқ‘Ү\|Q^{(2)}[\boldsymbol{r}^{(1)}](\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v})\|_{2}^{2}<T with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/10вҖӢtabsent1110рқ‘Ў\geq 1-1/10t over the Gaussian рқ‘®рқ‘®\boldsymbol{G}. In the second round, we restrict our analysis of the algorithm to only those (u,v)рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј(u,v) which satisfy (2). We again define a distribution wвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ӨвҖІw^{\prime} over the inputs and for each such (u,v)рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј(u,v) we define a distribution PuвҖӢvsubscriptрқ‘ғрқ‘ўрқ‘ЈP_{uv} over the round 111 and round 222 responses received by the algorithm. We define a new loss function with parameter TвҖІ=О”вӢ…Tsuperscriptрқ‘ҮвҖІвӢ…О”рқ‘ҮT^{\prime}=\Delta\cdot T for a multiplicative factor О”О”\Delta and again obtain a statement similar to (2) for a large fraction of inputs (u,v)рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј(u,v) and repeat a similar argument for tрқ‘Ўt rounds and show that there is an О©вҖӢ(1)О©1\Omega(1) fraction of the inputs for which the squared norm of the projection of uвҠ—vtensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Јu\otimes v onto the query space after tрқ‘Ўt rounds is bounded by TвҖӢ(t)рқ‘Үрқ‘ЎT(t) with high probability over the Gaussian part of the input. This gives the result in TheoremВ 3.4. Note that вҖ–рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—вҖ–22=О©вҖӢ(n2)superscriptsubscriptnormtensor-productрқ’–рқ’—22О©superscriptрқ‘ӣ2\|\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v}\|_{2}^{2}=\Omega(n^{2}) with high probability and for any fixed matrix Qрқ‘„Q with kрқ‘ҳk orthonormal rows, EвҒЎ[вҖ–QвҖӢ(рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—)вҖ–22]=kEsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘„tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—22рқ‘ҳ\operatorname{E}[\|Q(\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v})\|_{2}^{2}]=k which corresponds to the amount of вҖңinformationвҖқ the algorithm starts with. As we show that the вҖңinformationвҖқ in each round grows by some multiplicative factor О”О”\Delta, a number О©вҖӢ(logО”вҒЎ(n2/k))О©subscriptО”superscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳ\Omega(\log_{\Delta}(n^{2}/k)) of rounds is required to obtain an вҖңinformationвҖқ of ОҳвҖӢ(n2)Оҳsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2\Theta(n^{2}), which is how we obtain our lower bounds. Here information is measured as the squared projection of рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v} onto the query space of the algorithm.

We also extend our results to identifying a rank rрқ‘ҹr spike (sum of rрқ‘ҹr random outer products) corrupted by Gaussian noise. Specifically, we consider the random matrix рқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} where all the coordinates of рқ‘®,рқ’–i,рқ’—iрқ‘®subscriptрқ’–рқ‘–subscriptрқ’—рқ‘–\boldsymbol{G},\boldsymbol{u}_{i},\boldsymbol{v}_{i} are independently sampled from NвҖӢ(0,1)рқ‘Ғ01N(0,1). We show that if there is an algorithm that uses kрқ‘ҳk iterations in each round and identifies the spike with probability вүҘ9/10absent910\geq 9/10, then it must run for О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n2/k)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎn)О©superscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\Omega(\log(n^{2}/k)/\log\log n) rounds by appealing to the lower bound we described above for the case of r=1рқ‘ҹ1r=1. We show that if there is an algorithm for r>1рқ‘ҹ1r>1 that requires t<OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n2/k)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎn)рқ‘Ўрқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣt<O(\log(n^{2}/k)/\log\log n) adaptive rounds, then it can be used to solve the rank 111 spike estimation problem in tрқ‘Ўt rounds as well which contradicts the lower bound.

We then provide lower bounds on approximate algorithms for a host of problems such as spectral norm low rank approximation (LRA), Schatten norm LRA, Ky-Fan norm LRA and reduced rank regression, by showing that algorithms to solve these problems can be used to estimate the spike рқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} in the random matrix рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}, and then use the aforementioned lower bounds on algorithms that can estimate the spike. Although our hard distribution is supported on non-symmetric matrices, we are still able to obtain lower bounds for algorithms for spectral norm LRA (rank rвүҘ2рқ‘ҹ2r\geq 2) for symmetric matrices as well by considering a suitably defined symmetric random matrix using our hard distribution. Let рқ‘Ёвү”рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івү”рқ‘Ёрқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{A}\coloneqq\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} be the hard distribution in the case of rank r=1рқ‘ҹ1r=1. We symmetrize the matrix by considering, рқ‘Ёsym=[0рқ‘Ёрқ‘Ёрқ–і0]subscriptрқ‘Ёsymmatrix0рқ‘Ёsuperscriptрқ‘Ёрқ–і0\boldsymbol{A}_{\text{sym}}=\begin{bmatrix}0&\boldsymbol{A}\\\boldsymbol{A}^{\mathsf{T}}&0\end{bmatrix}. This symmetrization, as opposed to рқ‘ЁвҖӢрқ‘Ёрқ–ірқ‘Ёsuperscriptрқ‘Ёрқ–і\boldsymbol{A}\boldsymbol{A}^{\mathsf{T}} or рқ‘Ёрқ–івҖӢрқ‘Ёsuperscriptрқ‘Ёрқ–ірқ‘Ё\boldsymbol{A}^{\mathsf{T}}\boldsymbol{A}, has the advantage that a linear measurement of рқ‘Ёsymsubscriptрқ‘Ёsym\boldsymbol{A}_{\text{sym}} can be obtained from an appropriately transformed linear measurement of рқ‘Ёрқ‘Ё\boldsymbol{A}, thereby letting us obtain lower bounds for symmetric instances as well in the linear measurements model. However, we cannot obtain lower bounds for rank 111 spectral norm LRA for symmetric matrices using this symmetrization as the top two singular values of рқ‘Ёsymsubscriptрқ‘Ёsym\boldsymbol{A}_{\text{sym}} are equal and hence even a zero matrix is a perfect rank 111 spectral norm LRA for рқ‘Ёsymsubscriptрқ‘Ёsym\boldsymbol{A}_{\text{sym}} which does not give any information about the plant рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v}.

As discussed, low rank matrix recovery has been extensively studied (see [5] and references therein for earlier work). Relatedly, [13] study the Robust PCA problem where the aim is to estimate the sum of a low rank matrix and a sparse matrix from noisy vector products with the hidden matrix. [30] study the Robust PCA problem when given access to linear measurements with the hidden matrix.

For non-adaptive algorithms for low rank matrix recovery with Gaussian errors, [5] show that their selectors based on the restricted isometry property of measurement matrices are optimal up to constant factors in the minimax error sense when the noise follows a Gaussian distribution. Our TheoremВ 1.1 extends their lower bounds and shows that if there is any randomized measurement matrix222Note that we assume a measurement matrix has orthonormal rows and that each measurement is corrupted by Gaussian noise of variance 111 рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} with kрқ‘ҳk rows coupled with a recovery algorithm that outputs a reconstruction for any rank rрқ‘ҹr matrix with вҖ–AвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2=ОҳвҖӢ(nвҖӢr)superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқ–Ҙ2Оҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹ\|A\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}=\Theta(nr), then it must have k=О©вҖӢ(n2вҲ’oвҖӢ(1))рқ‘ҳО©superscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ң1k=\Omega(n^{2-o(1)}). We again note that we give lower bounds even for algorithms with multiple adaptive rounds.

Our technique to show lower bounds is to plant a low rank matrix (Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1ruiвҖӢviрқ–ірқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–і(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} in an nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n Gaussian matrix so that any вҖңorthonormalвҖқ access to the plant is corrupted by independent Gaussian noise. Notably this technique has been employed to obtain lower bounds on adaptive algorithms for sparse recovery in [23]. Even in the non-adaptive setting, Li and Woodruff [18] use the same hard distribution as we do to obtain sketching lower bounds for approximating Schatten pрқ‘қp norms, the operator norm, and the Ky Fan norms. The technique to show their lower bounds is that if a sketching matrix has kвүӨc/(r2вҖӢs4)рқ‘ҳрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ҹ2superscriptрқ‘ 4k\leq c/(r^{2}s^{4}) rows333Their lower bound is a bit more general but we state this formulation for simplicity., it cannot distinguish between the random matrix рқ‘®рқ‘®\boldsymbol{G} and the random matrix рқ‘®+sвҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқ‘®рқ‘ superscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+s\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} where all the coordinates of рқ‘®,рқ’–i,рқ’—iрқ‘®subscriptрқ’–рқ‘–subscriptрқ’—рқ‘–\boldsymbol{G},\boldsymbol{u}_{i},\boldsymbol{v}_{i} are drawn uniformly at random. They prove this by showing that dTVвҖӢ(в„’1,в„’2)subscriptрқ‘‘TVsubscriptв„’1subscriptв„’2d_{\textnormal{TV}}(\mathcal{L}_{1},\mathcal{L}_{2}) is small if в„’1subscriptв„’1\mathcal{L}_{1} is the distribution of MвӢ…vecвҒЎ(рқ‘®)вӢ…рқ‘Җvecрқ‘®M\cdot\operatorname{vec}(\boldsymbol{G}) and в„’2subscriptв„’2\mathcal{L}_{2} is the distribution of MвҖӢvecвҒЎ(рқ‘®+sвҖӢвҲ‘i=1nрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–і)рқ‘Җvecрқ‘®рқ‘ superscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–іM\operatorname{vec}(\boldsymbol{G}+s\sum_{i=1}^{n}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}) for any fixed measurement matrix Mрқ‘ҖM with kвүӨc/(r2вҖӢs4)рқ‘ҳрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ҹ2superscriptрқ‘ 4k\leq c/(r^{2}s^{4}) rows. Their techniques do not extend to the plant estimation in the distribution рқ‘®+sвҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқ‘®рқ‘ superscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+s\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} as the statement they prove only says that over the randomness of рқ‘®,рқ’–i,рқ’—iрқ‘®subscriptрқ’–рқ‘–subscriptрқ’—рқ‘–\boldsymbol{G},\boldsymbol{u}_{i},\boldsymbol{v}_{i}, the response distribution for рқ‘®+sвҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқ‘®рқ‘ superscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+s\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} is close to the response distribution for рқ‘®рқ‘®\boldsymbol{G}, but in our case, we want the distributions в„’u,vsubscriptв„’рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј\mathcal{L}_{u,v} and в„’uвҖІ,vвҖІsubscriptв„’superscriptрқ‘ўвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ЈвҖІ\mathcal{L}_{u^{\prime},v^{\prime}} to be indistinguishable, where в„’u,vsubscriptв„’рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј\mathcal{L}_{u,v} is the response distribution for рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1uiвҖӢviрқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘–1subscriptрқ‘ўрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}u_{i}v_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}.

Later, [28] considered the distribution of the symmetric random matrix рқ‘ҫ+О»вҖӢрқ‘јвҖӢрқ‘јрқ–ірқ‘ҫрқңҶрқ‘јsuperscriptрқ‘јрқ–і\boldsymbol{W}+\lambda\boldsymbol{U}\boldsymbol{U}^{\mathsf{T}}, where рқ‘ҫрқ‘ҫ\boldsymbol{W} is the nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n symmetric Wigner matrix (рқ‘®+рқ‘®рқ–і)/2рқ‘®superscriptрқ‘®рқ–і2(\boldsymbol{G}+\boldsymbol{G}^{\mathsf{T}})/\sqrt{2} and рқ‘јрқ‘ј\boldsymbol{U} is a uniformly random nГ—rрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹn\times r matrix with orthonormal columns. They focus on obtaining lower bounds on adaptive algorithms that estimate the spike рқ‘јрқ‘ј\boldsymbol{U} in the matrix-vector product model. In particular, they show that if Qрқ‘„Q is a basis for the query space spanned by any deterministic algorithm after querying kрқ‘ҳk adaptive matrix-vector queries, then О»rвҖӢ(Qрқ–івҖӢрқ‘јвҖӢрқ‘јрқ–івҖӢQ)subscriptрқңҶрқ‘ҹsuperscriptрқ‘„рқ–ірқ‘јsuperscriptрқ‘јрқ–ірқ‘„\lambda_{r}(Q^{\mathsf{T}}\boldsymbol{U}\boldsymbol{U}^{\mathsf{T}}Q) grows as вҲјО»k/rsimilar-toabsentsuperscriptрқңҶрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҹ\sim\lambda^{k/r}. Using this, they show that any algorithm which, given access to an arbitrary symmetric matrix AрқҗҙA in the matrix-vector product query model, must use О©вҖӢ(rвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n)/gap)О©рқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣgap\Omega(r\log(n)/\sqrt{\text{gap}}) adaptive queries to output an nГ—rрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹn\times r orthonormal matrix Vрқ‘үV satisfying, for a small enough constant cрқ‘җc,вҹЁV,AвҖӢVвҹ©вүҘ(1вҲ’cвӢ…gap)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1rО»iвҖӢ(A),рқ‘үрқҗҙрқ‘ү1вӢ…рқ‘җgapsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқңҶрқ‘–рқҗҙ\displaystyle\langle V,AV\rangle\geq(1-c\cdot\text{gap})\sum_{i=1}^{r}\lambda_{i}(A),(3)where gap=(О»rвҖӢ(A)вҲ’О»r+1вҖӢ(A))/О»rвҖӢ(A)gapsubscriptрқңҶрқ‘ҹрқҗҙsubscriptрқңҶрқ‘ҹ1рқҗҙsubscriptрқңҶрқ‘ҹрқҗҙ\text{gap}=(\lambda_{r}(A)-\lambda_{r+1}(A))/\lambda_{r}(A). We note the above guarantee is non-standard in the low rank approximation literature, which instead focuses more on approximation algorithms for Frobenius norm and spectral norm LRA. While in the matrix-vector product model, their hard distribution helps in getting lower bounds for numerical linear algebra problems on symmetric matrices, it seems that our hard distribution рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}} is easier to understand in the linear measurement model and gives the important property that the noise between rounds is independent, which is what lets us reduce the matrix-recovery problem with noisy measurements to spike estimation in рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}.

Recently, Bakshi and Narayanan [1] obtained a tight lower bound for rank-111 spectral norm low rank approximation problem in the matrix-vector product model. They show that О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎn/Оө)О©рқ‘ӣрқңҖ\Omega(\log n/\sqrt{\varepsilon}) matrix vector products are required to obtain a 1+Оө1рқңҖ1+\varepsilon spectral norm low rank approximation. We stress that while our results are not for 1+Оө1рқңҖ1+\varepsilon approximations, they hold in the stronger linear measurements model.

Given an integer nвүҘ1рқ‘ӣ1n\geq 1, we use [n]delimited-[]рқ‘ӣ[n] to denote the set {1,вҖҰ,n}1вҖҰрқ‘ӣ\set{1,\ldots,n}. For a vector vвҲҲв„қnрқ‘Јsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣv\in\mathbb{R}^{n}, вҖ–vвҖ–2вү”(вҲ‘iвҲҲ[n]vi2)1/2вү”subscriptnormрқ‘Ј2superscriptsubscriptрқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–212\|v\|_{2}\coloneqq(\sum_{i\in[n]}v_{i}^{2})^{1/2} denotes the Euclidean norm. For a matrix AвҲҲв„қnГ—dрқҗҙsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘A\in\mathbb{R}^{n\times d}, вҖ–AвҖ–рқ–Ҙsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқ–Ҙ\|A\|_{\mathsf{F}} denotes the Frobenius norm (вҲ‘i,jAiвҖӢj2)1/2superscriptsubscriptрқ‘–рқ‘—superscriptsubscriptрқҗҙрқ‘–рқ‘—212(\sum_{i,j}A_{ij}^{2})^{1/2} and вҖ–AвҖ–2subscriptnormрқҗҙ2\|A\|_{2} denotes the spectral norm supxвү 0вҖ–AвҖӢxвҖ–2/вҖ–xвҖ–2subscriptsupremumрқ‘Ҙ0subscriptnormрқҗҙрқ‘Ҙ2subscriptnormрқ‘Ҙ2\sup_{x\neq 0}\|Ax\|_{2}/\|x\|_{2}. For pвүҘ2рқ‘қ2p\geq 2, we use вҖ–AвҖ–рқ–Іpsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptрқ–Ірқ‘қ\|A\|_{\mathsf{S}_{p}} to denote the Schatten-pрқ‘қp norm (вҲ‘iПғip)1/psuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘–рқ‘қ1рқ‘қ(\sum_{i}\sigma_{i}^{p})^{1/p} and for pвҲҲ[minвҒЎ(n,d)]рқ‘қdelimited-[]рқ‘ӣрқ‘‘p\in[\min(n,d)], we use вҖ–AвҖ–рқ–Ҙpsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptрқ–Ҙрқ‘қ\|A\|_{\mathsf{F}_{p}} to denote the Ky-Fan pрқ‘қp norm вҲ‘i=1pПғisuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘қsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘–\sum_{i=1}^{p}\sigma_{i}, where Пғ1,вҖҰ,ПғminвҒЎ(n,d)subscriptрқңҺ1вҖҰsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘\sigma_{1},\ldots,\sigma_{\min(n,d)} denote the singular values of the matrix AрқҗҙA. Given a parameter kрқ‘ҳk, the matrix [A]ksubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗҙрқ‘ҳ[A]_{k} denotes the best rank kрқ‘ҳk approximation for matrix AрқҗҙA in Frobenius norm. By the Eckart-Young-Mirsky theorem, the best rank kрқ‘ҳk approximation under any unitarily invariant norm, which includes the spectral norm, Frobenius norm, Schatten norms and Ky-Fan norms, is given by truncating the Singular Value Decomposition of the matrix AрқҗҙA to top kрқ‘ҳk singular values.

Let ОҳОҳ\Theta be a set of parameters and рқ’«={PОё:ОёвҲҲОҳ}рқ’«:subscriptрқ‘ғрқңғрқңғОҳ\mathcal{P}=\set{P_{\theta}\,:\,\theta\in\Theta} be a set of distributions over рқ’ірқ’і\mathcal{X}. Let wрқ‘Өw be the prior distribution on ОҳОҳ\Theta known to a learner. Suppose ОёвҲјwsimilar-toрқңғрқ‘Ө\theta\sim w, and xвҲјPОёsimilar-toрқ‘Ҙsubscriptрқ‘ғрқңғx\sim P_{\theta} and that the learner is given xрқ‘Ҙx. Now the learner wants to learn some information about Оёрқңғ\theta. Let рқ”Ў:рқ’івҶ’рқ’ң:рқ”ЎвҶ’рқ’ірқ’ң\mathfrak{d}:\mathcal{X}\rightarrow\mathcal{A} be a mapping from sample xрқ‘Ҙx to action space рқ’ңрқ’ң\mathcal{A} and L:ОҳГ—рқ’ңвҶ’{0,1}:рқҗҝвҶ’Оҳрқ’ң01L:\Theta\times\mathcal{A}\rightarrow\set{0,1} be a zero-one loss function. We defineRBayesвҖӢ(L,Оҳ,w)=infрқ”ЎвҲ«ОҳExвҲјPОёвҒЎ[LвҖӢ(Оё,рқ”ЎвҖӢ(x))]вҖӢwвҖӢ(dвҖӢОё)=infрқ”ЎEОёвҲјwвҖӢ[ExвҲјPОёвҒЎLвҖӢ(Оё,рқ”ЎвҖӢ(x))],subscriptрқ‘…BayesрқҗҝОҳрқ‘Өsubscriptinfimumрқ”ЎsubscriptОҳsubscriptEsimilar-toрқ‘Ҙsubscriptрқ‘ғрқңғрқҗҝрқңғрқ”Ўрқ‘Ҙрқ‘Өрқ‘‘рқңғsubscriptinfimumрқ”Ўsubscriptрқҗёsimilar-toрқңғрқ‘Өdelimited-[]subscriptEsimilar-toрқ‘Ҙsubscriptрқ‘ғрқңғрқҗҝрқңғрқ”Ўрқ‘ҘR_{\text{Bayes}}(L,\Theta,w)=\inf_{\mathfrak{d}}\int_{\Theta}\operatorname{E}_{x\sim P_{\theta}}[L(\theta,\mathfrak{d}(x))]w(d\theta)=\inf_{\mathfrak{d}}E_{\theta\sim w}[\operatorname{E}_{x\sim P_{\theta}}L(\theta,\mathfrak{d}(x))],andR0вҖӢ(L,Оҳ,w)=infaвҲҲрқ’ңвҲ«ОҳLвҖӢ(Оё,a)вҖӢwвҖӢ(dвҖӢОё)=infaвҲҲрқ’ңEОёвҲјwвҒЎ[LвҖӢ(Оё,a)].subscriptрқ‘…0рқҗҝОҳрқ‘Өsubscriptinfimumрқ‘Һрқ’ңsubscriptОҳрқҗҝрқңғрқ‘Һрқ‘Өрқ‘‘рқңғsubscriptinfimumрқ‘Һрқ’ңsubscriptEsimilar-toрқңғрқ‘Өрқҗҝрқңғрқ‘ҺR_{0}(L,\Theta,w)=\inf_{a\in\mathcal{A}}\int_{\Theta}L(\theta,a)w(d\theta)=\inf_{a\in\mathcal{A}}\operatorname{E}_{\theta\sim w}[L(\theta,a)].We drop ОҳОҳ\Theta from the notation when it is clear.

Let рқ’һрқ’һ\mathcal{C} denote the set of all convex functions fрқ‘“f with fвҖӢ(1)=0рқ‘“10f(1)=0. Let Pрқ‘ғP and Qрқ‘„Q be two distributions with densities pрқ‘қp and qрқ‘һq over a common measure ОјрқңҮ\mu. Then we have the fрқ‘“f-divergence DfвҖӢ(PвҲҘQ)subscriptрқҗ·рқ‘“conditionalрқ‘ғрқ‘„D_{f}(P\|Q) defined asDfвҖӢ(PвҲҘQ)=вҲ«fвҖӢ(pq)вҖӢqвҖӢрқ‘‘Ој+fвҖІвҖӢ(вҲһ)вҖӢPвҖӢ{q=0}subscriptрқҗ·рқ‘“conditionalрқ‘ғрқ‘„рқ‘“рқ‘қрқ‘һрқ‘һdifferential-dрқңҮsuperscriptрқ‘“вҖІрқ‘ғрқ‘һ0D_{f}(P\|Q)=\int f\left(\frac{p}{q}\right)qd\mu+f^{\prime}(\infty)P\set{q=0}using the convention 0вӢ…вҲһ=вҲһвӢ…00\cdot\infty=\infty. For f=xвҖӢlogвҒЎ(x)рқ‘“рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ҙf=x\log(x), the fрқ‘“f-divergence DfвҖӢ(PвҲҘQ)=dKLвҖӢ(PвҲҘQ)subscriptрқҗ·рқ‘“conditionalрқ‘ғрқ‘„subscriptрқ‘‘KLconditionalрқ‘ғрқ‘„D_{f}(P\|Q)=d_{\textnormal{KL}}(P\|Q), the KullbackвҖ“Leibler (KL) divergence. We frequently use dKLвҖӢ(рқ‘ҝвҲҘрқ’Җ)subscriptрқ‘‘KLconditionalрқ‘ҝрқ’Җd_{\textnormal{KL}}(\boldsymbol{X}\|\boldsymbol{Y}) for some random variables рқ‘ҝрқ‘ҝ\boldsymbol{X} and рқ’Җрқ’Җ\boldsymbol{Y}, which means the KL divergence between the distributions of рқ‘ҝрқ‘ҝ\boldsymbol{X} and рқ’Җрқ’Җ\boldsymbol{Y}.

Now we can define the fрқ‘“f-informativity of a set of distributions рқ’«рқ’«\mathcal{P} with respect to a distribution wрқ‘Өw as follows:IfвҖӢ(рқ’«,w)=infQвҲ«DfвҖӢ(PОёвҲҘQ)вҖӢwвҖӢ(dвҖӢОё)=infQEОёвҲјwвҒЎ[DfвҖӢ(PОёвҲҘQ)].subscriptрқҗјрқ‘“рқ’«рқ‘Өsubscriptinfimumрқ‘„subscriptрқҗ·рқ‘“conditionalsubscriptрқ‘ғрқңғрқ‘„рқ‘Өрқ‘‘рқңғsubscriptinfimumрқ‘„subscriptEsimilar-toрқңғрқ‘Өsubscriptрқҗ·рқ‘“conditionalsubscriptрқ‘ғрқңғрқ‘„I_{f}(\mathcal{P},w)=\inf_{Q}\int D_{f}(P_{\theta}\|Q)w(d\theta)=\inf_{Q}\operatorname{E}_{\theta\sim w}[D_{f}(P_{\theta}\|Q)].We use IвҖӢ(рқ’«,w)рқҗјрқ’«рқ‘ӨI(\mathcal{P},w) to denote the fрқ‘“f-informativity for f=xвҖӢlogвҒЎxрқ‘“рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ҙf=x\log x.We finally have the following theorem from [7].

We state some properties of the KL-divergence that we use throughout the paper.

For xвҲҲв„°рқ‘Ҙв„°x\in\mathcal{E}, we have p~вҖӢ(x)=pвҖӢ(x)/PrвҒЎ[PвҲҲв„°]~рқ‘қрқ‘Ҙрқ‘қрқ‘ҘPrрқ‘ғв„°\tilde{p}(x)=p(x)/\Pr[P\in\mathcal{E}] and for xвҲүв„°рқ‘Ҙв„°x\not\in\mathcal{E}, p~вҖӢ(x)=0~рқ‘қрқ‘Ҙ0\tilde{p}(x)=0. See [26, 17] and references therein for proofs.

We now state the main theorem which shows a lower bound on the number of adaptive rounds required for any deterministic algorithm to estimate the plant when the input is a random matrix рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}. We use this theorem to prove TheoremВ 1.1 and lower bounds for other numerical linear algebra problems.

We prove the lower bound for the rank-rрқ‘ҹr plant estimation by first proving a lower bound on the rank-111 plant estimation and then reducing the rank-111 recovery problem to rank-rрқ‘ҹr recovery problem. For the rank-111 recovery problem, we prove the following lemma:

Setting Оі=OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n))рқӣҫрқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣ\gamma=O(\log(n)), the theorem shows that if tвүӨcвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)/(logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n)+logвҒЎ(Оұ))рқ‘Ўрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқӣјt\leq c\log(n^{2}/k)/(\log\log(n)+\log(\alpha)) for a small enough constant cрқ‘җc, then for any tрқ‘Ўt-round deterministic algorithm,Prрқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+sвҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івҒЎ[вҖ–QвҖӢ(рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—)вҖ–22вүӨn2/100]вүҘ4/5.subscriptPrрқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқ‘ рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–іsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘„tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—22superscriptрқ‘ӣ210045\displaystyle\Pr_{\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+s\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}}[\|Q(\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v})\|_{2}^{2}\leq n^{2}/100]\geq 4/5.(4)Setting Оі=OвҖӢ(1)рқӣҫрқ‘Ӯ1\gamma=O(1), we obtain that if tвүӨcвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)/(logвҒЎ(Оұ))рқ‘Ўрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқӣјt\leq c\log(n^{2}/k)/(\log(\alpha)) for a small enough constant cрқ‘җc, thenPrрқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+sвҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івҒЎ[вҖ–QвҖӢ(рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—)вҖ–22вүӨn2/100]вүҘ1/polyвҒЎ(n).subscriptPrрқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқ‘ рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–іsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘„tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—22superscriptрқ‘ӣ21001polyрқ‘ӣ\displaystyle\Pr_{\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+s\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}}[\|Q(\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v})\|_{2}^{2}\leq n^{2}/100]\geq 1/\operatorname{poly}(n).(5)The above lemma directly shows lower bounds on any deterministic algorithm that can approximate the rank-111 planted matrix.

Before proceeding to the proof, we first discuss some notation, distributions and random variables that we use throughout the proof. Fix an arbitrary deterministic algorithm Alg. Let A=G+sвҖӢuвҖӢvрқ–ірқҗҙрқҗәрқ‘ рқ‘ўsuperscriptрқ‘Јрқ–іA=G+suv^{\mathsf{T}} be a fixed realization of the random matrix рқ‘Ёрқ‘Ё\boldsymbol{A}. Recall s=Оұ/nрқ‘ рқӣјрқ‘ӣs=\alpha/\sqrt{n}. The algorithm Alg queries a fixed orthonormal matrix Q(1)superscriptрқ‘„1Q^{(1)} and receives the response r(1)вү”Q(1)вҖӢvecвҒЎ(A)=Q(1)вҖӢg+sвҖӢQ(1)вҖӢ(uвҠ—v)вү”superscriptрқ‘ҹ1superscriptрқ‘„1vecрқҗҙsuperscriptрқ‘„1рқ‘”рқ‘ superscriptрқ‘„1tensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Јr^{(1)}\coloneqq Q^{(1)}\operatorname{vec}(A)=Q^{(1)}g+sQ^{(1)}(u\otimes v) where we use gвү”vecвҒЎ(G)вү”рқ‘”vecрқҗәg\coloneqq\operatorname{vec}(G). As Alg is deterministic, in the second round it queries the matrix Q(2)вҖӢ[r(1)]superscriptрқ‘„2delimited-[]superscriptрқ‘ҹ1Q^{(2)}[r^{(1)}]. We show that the lower bounds on number of linear measurements required to estimate the rank-111 planted matrix can be extended to algorithms that estimate the rank-rрқ‘ҹr planted matrix as well.

Using the reduction from matrix recovery with noisy measurements to plant estimation with exact measurements that we described in the previous sections, we can now prove TheoremВ 1.1.

We prove the following helper lemma that we use in our proof.

As AрқҗҙA has rank at most rрқ‘ҹr, we have tвүҘвҖ–AвҲ’BвҖ–2вүҘвҖ–BвҲ’[B]rвҖ–2рқ‘Ўsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗө2subscriptnormрқҗөsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗөрқ‘ҹ2t\geq\|A-B\|_{2}\geq\|B-[B]_{r}\|_{2}. Thus, вҖ–AвҲ’[B]rвҖ–2вүӨвҖ–AвҲ’BвҖ–2+вҖ–BвҲ’[B]rвҖ–2вүӨ2вҖӢtsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗөрқ‘ҹ2subscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗө2subscriptnormрқҗөsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗөрқ‘ҹ22рқ‘Ў\|A-[B]_{r}\|_{2}\leq\|A-B\|_{2}+\|B-[B]_{r}\|_{2}\leq 2t.вҲҺ

By a standard reduction, it suffices to show that there is a distribution on nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n matrices for which any tрқ‘Ўt-round deterministic algorithm which makes kрқ‘ҳk general linear measurements in each round and outputs a 222-approximate spectral rank approximation satisfies tвүҘcвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n)рқ‘Ўрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣt\geq c\log(n^{2}/k)/\log\log(n).

Consider the nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n random matrix рқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+sвҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқ‘ рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+s\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} for s=500/nрқ‘ 500рқ‘ӣs=500/\sqrt{n}.
