The following theorem states our lower bound for algorithms which output a spectral LRA for each matrix with high probability.

The proof of this lemma is similar to that of TheoremВ 5.1. The existence of a randomized tрқ‘Ўt round algorithm that outputs a 2-approximate spectral norm LRA for every instance with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/polyвҒЎ(n)absent11polyрқ‘ӣ\geq 1-1/\operatorname{poly}(n) implies the existence of a deterministic algorithm that outputs a 2-approximate spectral norm LRA with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/polyвҒЎ(n)absent11polyрқ‘ӣ\geq 1-1/\operatorname{poly}(n) over the distribution of рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}. As in the proof of the TheoremВ 5.1, this algorithm can be used to construct a t+1рқ‘Ў1t+1 round algorithm that with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/polyвҒЎ(n)absent11polyрқ‘ӣ\geq 1-1/\operatorname{poly}(n) over the matrix рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}, computes a unit vector qрқ‘һq satisfyingвҹЁq,рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—вҹ©2вүҘn2/64.superscriptрқ‘һtensor-productрқ’–рқ’—2superscriptрқ‘ӣ264\displaystyle\langle q,\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v}\rangle^{2}\geq n^{2}/64.Now, (5) implies that t+1вүҘcвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)рқ‘Ў1рқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳt+1\geq c\log(n^{2}/k) for a small enough constant cрқ‘җc.вҲҺ

For the random matrix рқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} for a large enough constant Оұрқӣј\alpha considered in the above theorem, we have that (Пғ1вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙ)/Пғ2вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙ))вүҘ2subscriptрқңҺ1рқ‘ҙsubscriptрқңҺ2рқ‘ҙ2(\sigma_{1}(\boldsymbol{M})/\sigma_{2}(\boldsymbol{M}))\geq 2 with high probability. Now consider the random matrixрқ‘ҙвҖІ=[рқ‘ҙ003вҖӢnвҖӢОұвҖӢIrвҲ’1].superscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІmatrixрқ‘ҙ003рқ‘ӣрқӣјsubscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҹ1\displaystyle\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime}=\begin{bmatrix}\boldsymbol{M}&0\\0&3\sqrt{n}\alpha I_{r-1}\end{bmatrix}.With high probability, we have ПғrвҖӢ(рқ‘ҙвҖІ)=Пғ1вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙ)вүҘ(Оұ/2)вҖӢnsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹsuperscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІsubscriptрқңҺ1рқ‘ҙрқӣј2рқ‘ӣ\sigma_{r}(\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime})=\sigma_{1}(\boldsymbol{M})\geq(\alpha/2)\sqrt{n} and Пғr+1вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙвҖІ)=Пғ2вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙ)вүӨ2вҖӢnsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1superscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІsubscriptрқңҺ2рқ‘ҙ2рқ‘ӣ\sigma_{r+1}(\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime})=\sigma_{2}(\boldsymbol{M})\leq 2\sqrt{n} implying Пғr+1вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙвҖІ)/ПғrвҖӢ(рқ‘ҙвҖІ)вүӨ1/2subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1superscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹsuperscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІ12\sigma_{r+1}(\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime})/\sigma_{r}(\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime})\leq 1/2. A proof similar to that of the above theorem now shows that algorithms using kвүҘnвҖӢrрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹk\geq nr general linear measurements in each round and outputting a 222-approximate rank-rрқ‘ҹr LRA with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/polyвҒЎ(n)absent11polyрқ‘ӣ\geq 1-1/\operatorname{poly}(n) for matrices Mрқ‘ҖM with Пғr+1вҖӢ(M)/ПғrвҖӢ(M)вүӨ1/2subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1рқ‘ҖsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹрқ‘Җ12\sigma_{r+1}(M)/\sigma_{r}(M)\leq 1/2 have a lower bound of О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n2/k))О©superscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳ\Omega(\log(n^{2}/k)) rounds. Moreover for kвүҘCвҖӢnвҖӢrрқ‘ҳрқҗ¶рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹk\geq Cnr for a large enough constant Cрқҗ¶C and r=OвҖӢ(1)рқ‘ҹрқ‘Ӯ1r=O(1), the randomized subspace iteration algorithm starting with a subspace of k/nрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣk/n-dimensions, after OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n2/k))рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳO(\log(n^{2}/k)) rounds outputs, with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/polyвҒЎ(n)absent11polyрқ‘ӣ\geq 1-1/\operatorname{poly}(n), a 222-approximate rank-rрқ‘ҹr spectral norm LRA for all matrices satisfying Пғr+1вҖӢ(M)/ПғrвҖӢ(M)вүӨ1/2subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1рқ‘ҖsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹрқ‘Җ12\sigma_{r+1}(M)/\sigma_{r}(M)\leq 1/2. See [12, TheoremВ 5.8] for a proof.

Note that the subspace iteration algorithm starting with a subspace of k/nрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣk/n-dimensions performs (k/n)вӢ…n=kвӢ…рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳ(k/n)\cdot n=k general linear measurements in each round. Thus for r=OвҖӢ(1)рқ‘ҹрқ‘Ӯ1r=O(1) and kвүҘCвҖӢnвҖӢrрқ‘ҳрқҗ¶рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹk\geq Cnr for a large enough constant Cрқҗ¶C, the lower bound of О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n2/k))О©superscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳ\Omega(\log(n^{2}/k)) rounds for high probability spectral norm LRA algorithms for вҖңwell-conditionedвҖқ (Пғr+1/ПғrвүӨ1/2subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ12\sigma_{r+1}/\sigma_{r}\leq 1/2) instances is tight up to constant factors and shows that general linear measurements offer no improvement over matrix-vector products for well-conditioned problems. Thus we have the following theorem.

An interesting property of the hard distributions from previous works [28, 3] is that those distributions are supported on symmetric matrices and they hence obtain lower bounds for algorithms that work even only on symmetric instances. Although our hard distribution is non-symmetric, we can construct a distribution supported only on symmetric matrices and show lower bounds on algorithms using generalized linear queries for symmetric matrices.

Consider the 2вҖӢnГ—2вҖӢn2рқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ӣ2n\times 2n random matrix рқ‘ҙвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІ\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime} defined asрқ‘ҙвҖІ=[0nГ—nрқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙрқ–і0nГ—n]superscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІmatrixsubscript0рқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҙsuperscriptрқ‘ҙрқ–іsubscript0рқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣ\displaystyle\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime}=\begin{bmatrix}0_{n\times n}&\boldsymbol{M}\\\boldsymbol{M}^{\mathsf{T}}&0_{n\times n}\end{bmatrix}where рқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+sвҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқ‘ рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+s\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} for s=500/nрқ‘ 500рқ‘ӣs=500/\sqrt{n} and all coordinates of рқ‘®,рқ’–,рқ’—рқ‘®рқ’–рқ’—\boldsymbol{G},\boldsymbol{u},\boldsymbol{v} are independent standard Gaussian random variables. We have that for iвҲҲ[n]рқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘ӣi\in[n], Пғ2вҖӢiвҲ’1вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙвҖІ)=Пғ2вҖӢiвҖӢ(рқ‘ҙвҖІ)=ПғiвҖӢ(рқ‘ҙ)subscriptрқңҺ2рқ‘–1superscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІsubscriptрқңҺ2рқ‘–superscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘–рқ‘ҙ\sigma_{2i-1}(\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime})=\sigma_{2i}(\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime})=\sigma_{i}(\boldsymbol{M}) and that any arbitrary kрқ‘ҳk generalized linear measurements of the matrix рқ‘ҙвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІ\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime} can be simulated using 2вҖӢk2рқ‘ҳ2k general linear measurements of рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M}. Now suppose an algorithm that uses kрқ‘ҳk general linear measurements in each round outputs a rank rвүҘ2рқ‘ҹ2r\geq 2 matrix KрқҗҫK satisfyingвҖ–рқ‘ҙвҖІвҲ’KвҖ–2вүӨ2вҖӢПғr+1вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙвҖІ)вүӨ2вҖӢПғ1вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙ).subscriptnormsuperscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІрқҗҫ22subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1superscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІ2subscriptрқңҺ1рқ‘ҙ\displaystyle\|\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime}-K\|_{2}\leq 2\sigma_{r+1}(\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime})\leq 2\sigma_{1}(\boldsymbol{M}).Let the matrix KрқҗҫK be of the formK=[K1K2K3K4]рқҗҫmatrixsubscriptрқҗҫ1subscriptрқҗҫ2subscriptрқҗҫ3subscriptрқҗҫ4\displaystyle K=\begin{bmatrix}K_{1}&K_{2}\\K_{3}&K_{4}\end{bmatrix}As any sub-matrix of KрқҗҫK has rank at most that of KрқҗҫK, we obtain that K2subscriptрқҗҫ2K_{2} is a rank-rрқ‘ҹr matrix satisfyingвҖ–рқ‘ҙвҲ’K2вҖ–2вүӨ2вҖӢПғ1вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙ).subscriptnormрқ‘ҙsubscriptрқҗҫ222subscriptрқңҺ1рқ‘ҙ\displaystyle\|\boldsymbol{M}-K_{2}\|_{2}\leq 2\sigma_{1}(\boldsymbol{M}).Thus, the existence of a tрқ‘Ўt-round deterministic algorithm that uses kрқ‘ҳk generalized queries in each round and outputs a constant factor approximation of rank rрқ‘ҹr, spectral norm LRA, for the random matrix рқ‘ҙвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІ\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime} with probability вүҘ99/100absent99100\geq 99/100 implies the existence of a tрқ‘Ўt-round algorithm that uses 2вҖӢk2рқ‘ҳ2k generalized queries in each round and outputs a constant factor approximation of rank-rрқ‘ҹr spectral norm LRA for the random matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} with probability вүҘ99/100absent99100\geq 99/100. Now, as in the proof of TheoremВ 5.1, we obtain thattвүҘcвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/2вҖӢk)logвҒЎlogвҒЎnвүҘcвҖІвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)logвҒЎlogвҒЎn.рқ‘Ўрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ22рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘җвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\displaystyle t\geq c\frac{\log(n^{2}/2k)}{\log\log n}\geq c^{\prime}\frac{\log(n^{2}/k)}{\log\log n}.We obtain the proof by appropriately scaling nрқ‘ӣn in the statement.вҲҺ

The above theorem proves lower bounds for algorithms that solve constant factor rank-rрқ‘ҹr spectral norm Low Rank Approximation (LRA) for all rвүҘ2рқ‘ҹ2r\geq 2 even for symmetric instances. This leaves open just a lower bound on algorithms solving rank 111 spectral norm LRA for symmetric instances.

We first note the following lemma which bounds the Schatten-pрқ‘қp norm of an nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n Gaussian matrix.

We now state the theorem that shows lower bounds for Schatten norm low rank approximation.

The proof is very similar to the proof of TheoremВ 5.1. Let рқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+sвҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқ‘ рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+s\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} for s=Оұ/nрқ‘ рқӣјрқ‘ӣs=\alpha/\sqrt{n} for Оұрқӣј\alpha to be chosen later. Let Alg be a tрқ‘Ўt-round deterministic algorithm that outputs a 2-approximate Schatten pрқ‘қp-norm low rank approximation for рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} with probability вүҘ99/100absent99100\geq 99/100 over рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M}. Then we haveвҖ–рқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івҲ’K/sвҖ–вүӨ3вҖӢвҖ–рқ‘®вҖ–рқ–Іpsnormрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–ірқҗҫрқ‘ 3subscriptnormрқ‘®subscriptрқ–Ірқ‘қрқ‘ \displaystyle\|{\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}-K/s}\|\leq\frac{3\|\boldsymbol{G}\|_{\mathsf{S}_{p}}}{s}as minrank-вҖӢrвҖӢXвҒЎвҖ–рқ‘®+sвҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івҲ’XвҖ–рқ–ІpвүӨвҖ–рқ‘®вҖ–рқ–Іpsubscriptrank-рқ‘ҹрқ‘Ӣsubscriptnormрқ‘®рқ‘ рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘Ӣsubscriptрқ–Ірқ‘қsubscriptnormрқ‘®subscriptрқ–Ірқ‘қ\min_{\text{rank-}r\,X}\|\boldsymbol{G}+s\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}-X\|_{\mathsf{S}_{p}}\leq\|\boldsymbol{G}\|_{\mathsf{S}_{p}}. Using LemmaВ 5.6, with probability вүҘ9/10absent910\geq 9/10 over рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M}, we have thatвҖ–вҲ‘iрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–івҲ’K/sвҖ–рқ–ІpвүӨ90вҖӢn1+1/p/Оұ.subscriptnormsubscriptрқ‘–subscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–ірқҗҫрқ‘ subscriptрқ–Ірқ‘қ90superscriptрқ‘ӣ11рқ‘қрқӣј\displaystyle\|\sum_{i}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}-K/s\|_{\mathsf{S}_{p}}\leq 90n^{1+1/p}/\alpha.By picking Оұ=BвҖӢn1/pрқӣјрқҗөsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ1рқ‘қ\alpha=Bn^{1/p} for a large enough constant BрқҗөB, we obtain thatвҖ–рқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івҲ’K/sвҖ–2вүӨвҖ–рқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івҲ’K/sвҖ–рқ–ІpвүӨ(9/250)вҖӢn.subscriptnormрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–ірқҗҫрқ‘ 2subscriptnormрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–ірқҗҫрқ‘ subscriptрқ–Ірқ‘қ9250рқ‘ӣ\displaystyle\|\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}-K/s\|_{2}\leq\|\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}-K/s\|_{\mathsf{S}_{p}}\leq(9/250)n.Similar to the proof of TheoremВ 5.1, we can construct a unit vector qвҲҲв„қn2рқ‘һsuperscriptв„қsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2q\in\mathbb{R}^{n^{2}} such that with probability вүҘ8/10absent810\geq 8/10 over рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M}, we haveвҹЁq,рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—вҹ©2вүҘn2/64.superscriptрқ‘һtensor-productрқ’–рқ’—2superscriptрқ‘ӣ264\displaystyle\langle q,\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v}\rangle^{2}\geq n^{2}/64.Using (4), we obtain thatt+1вүҘcвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)1+logвҒЎ(Оұ)+logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n)вүҘcвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)1+(1/p)вҖӢlogвҒЎ(n)+logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n).рқ‘Ў1рқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳ1рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳ11рқ‘қрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣt+1\geq c\frac{\log(n^{2}/k)}{1+\log(\alpha)+\log\log(n)}\geq c\frac{\log(n^{2}/k)}{1+(1/p)\log(n)+\log\log(n)}.вҲҺ

In particular, for p=OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n))рқ‘қрқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣp=O(\log(n)/\log\log(n)), this gives a lower bound of О©вҖӢ(pвҖӢ(2вҲ’logвҒЎ(k)/logвҒЎ(n)))О©рқ‘қ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\Omega(p(2-\log(k)/\log(n))) on the number of adaptive rounds required if an algorithm can query kрқ‘ҳk general linear measurements in each round. Recently, Bakshi, Clarkson and Woodruff [2, AlgorithmВ 2] gave an algorithm for Schatten-pрқ‘қp low rank approximation for arbitrary matrices that runs in OвҖӢ(p1/2вҖӢlogвҒЎ(n))рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқ‘қ12рқ‘ӣO(p^{1/2}\log(n))444Although their algorithm is stated to use rвҖӢp1/6вҖӢlog2вҒЎ(n)рқ‘ҹsuperscriptрқ‘қ16superscript2рқ‘ӣrp^{1/6}\log^{2}(n) matrix-vector products, this does not appear to have been optimized, and looking at the analysis it runs in at most p1/2вҖӢlogвҒЎ(n)superscriptрқ‘қ12рқ‘ӣp^{1/2}\log(n) iterations, where each round queries at most rрқ‘ҹr matrix-vector products. iterations to output a constant factor approximation. For instances with ПғrвҖӢ(A)/Пғr+1вҖӢ(A)=1+О©вҖӢ(1)subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹрқҗҙsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1рқҗҙ1О©1\sigma_{r}(A)/\sigma_{r+1}(A)=1+\Omega(1), Saibaba [27, TheoremВ 8] showed that randomized subspace iteration gives a constant factor approximation to rank-rрқ‘ҹr Schatten-pрқ‘қp norm LRA in OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n))рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣO(\log(n)) iterations using nвҖӢrрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹnr linear measurements in each round.

Again consider the same instance рқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+sвҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқ‘ рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+s\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} with s=Оұ/nрқ‘ рқӣјрқ‘ӣs=\alpha/\sqrt{n} for Оұрқӣј\alpha chosen later. If KрқҗҫK is a 222-approximate rank-rрқ‘ҹr low rank approximation of рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} in Ky-Fan pрқ‘қp norm, thenвҖ–рқ‘®+sвҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івҲ’KвҖ–рқ–ҘpвүӨ2вҖӢвҖ–рқ‘®вҖ–рқ–Ҙpsubscriptnormрқ‘®рқ‘ рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–ірқҗҫsubscriptрқ–Ҙрқ‘қ2subscriptnormрқ‘®subscriptрқ–Ҙрқ‘қ\|\boldsymbol{G}+s\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}-K\|_{\mathsf{F}_{p}}\leq 2\|\boldsymbol{G}\|_{\mathsf{F}_{p}}which by the triangle inequality implies thatвҖ–sвҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–івҲ’KвҖ–рқ–ҘpвүӨ3вҖӢвҖ–рқ‘®вҖ–рқ–Ҙp.subscriptnormрқ‘ superscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–ірқҗҫsubscriptрқ–Ҙрқ‘қ3subscriptnormрқ‘®subscriptрқ–Ҙрқ‘қ\|s\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}-K\|_{\mathsf{F}_{p}}\leq 3\|\boldsymbol{G}\|_{\mathsf{F}_{p}}. As вҖ–рқ‘®вҖ–2вүӨ2вҖӢnsubscriptnormрқ‘®22рқ‘ӣ\|\boldsymbol{G}\|_{2}\leq 2\sqrt{n} with high probability, we have that вҖ–рқ‘®вҖ–рқ–ҘpвүӨ2вҖӢpвҖӢnsubscriptnormрқ‘®subscriptрқ–Ҙрқ‘қ2рқ‘қрқ‘ӣ\|\boldsymbol{G}\|_{\mathsf{F}_{p}}\leq 2p\sqrt{n} with high probability. Thus,вҖ–sвҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–івҲ’K/sвҖ–2вүӨвҖ–sвҖӢвҲ‘i=1rрқ’–iвҖӢрқ’—iрқ–івҲ’K/sвҖ–рқ–ҘpвүӨ6вҖӢpвҖӢnОұ.subscriptnormрқ‘ superscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–ірқҗҫрқ‘ 2subscriptnormрқ‘ superscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1рқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ’–рқ‘–superscriptsubscriptрқ’—рқ‘–рқ–ірқҗҫрқ‘ subscriptрқ–Ҙрқ‘қ6рқ‘қрқ‘ӣрқӣј\displaystyle\|s\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}-K/s\|_{2}\leq\|s\sum_{i=1}^{r}\boldsymbol{u}_{i}\boldsymbol{v}_{i}^{\mathsf{T}}-K/s\|_{\mathsf{F}_{p}}\leq\frac{6pn}{\alpha}.Picking Оұ=BвҖӢpрқӣјрқҗөрқ‘қ\alpha=Bp for a large enough constant BрқҗөB, we obtain that using the matrix KрқҗҫK, we can construct a unit vector qрқ‘һq such that вҹЁq,рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—вҹ©2вүҘn2/64superscriptрқ‘һtensor-productрқ’–рқ’—2superscriptрқ‘ӣ264\langle q,\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v}\rangle^{2}\geq n^{2}/64, thus showing at=cвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)logвҒЎ(p)+logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n)рқ‘Ўрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘қрқ‘ӣ\displaystyle t=c\frac{\log(n^{2}/k)}{\log(p)+\log\log(n)}round lower bound on any algorithm that performs kрқ‘ҳk general linear measurements to output a 222-approximate rank-rрқ‘ҹr approximation in Ky-Fan pрқ‘қp norm.вҲҺ

For p=OвҖӢ(1)рқ‘қрқ‘Ӯ1p=O(1), the Block Krylov iteration algorithm [20] gives an OвҖӢ(1)рқ‘Ӯ1O(1) approximate solution to the rank-rрқ‘ҹr Ky-Fan norm low rank approximation problem in OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n))рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣO(\log(n)) rounds while querying nвҖӢrрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹnr general linear measurements in each round. Thus our lower bound on constant approximate algorithms for Ky-Fan norm LRA is optimal up to a logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n)рқ‘ӣ\log\log(n) factor for r,p=OвҖӢ(1)рқ‘ҹрқ‘қрқ‘Ӯ1r,p=O(1).

First, we prove the following helper lemma.

We use the fact [12, TheoemВ 3.4] that if a rank rрқ‘ҹr matrix satisfies вҖ–AвҲ’BвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2вүӨвҖ–AвҲ’[A]rвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2+О·superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗөрқ–Ҙ2superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗҙрқ‘ҹрқ–Ҙ2рқңӮ\|A-B\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}\leq\|A-[A]_{r}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}+\eta, then вҖ–AвҲ’BвҖ–22вүӨвҖ–AвҲ’[A]rвҖ–22+О·superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗө22superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗҙрқ‘ҹ22рқңӮ\|A-B\|_{2}^{2}\leq\|A-[A]_{r}\|_{2}^{2}+\eta. If BрқҗөB is a 1+1/(nвҲ’r)11рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹ1+1/(n-r) approximate solution for rank rрқ‘ҹr Frobenius norm LRA, we haveвҖ–AвҲ’BвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗөрқ–Ҙ2\displaystyle\|A-B\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}вүӨ(1+1nвҲ’r)вҖӢвҖ–AвҲ’[A]rвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2absent11рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗҙрқ‘ҹрқ–Ҙ2\displaystyle\leq\left(1+\frac{1}{n-r}\right)\|A-[A]_{r}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}вүӨвҖ–AвҲ’[A]rвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2+Пғr+1вҖӢ(A)2+вҖҰ+ПғnвҖӢ(A)2nвҲ’rabsentsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗҙрқ‘ҹрқ–Ҙ2subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1superscriptрқҗҙ2вҖҰsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗҙ2рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹ\displaystyle\leq\|A-[A]_{r}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}+\frac{\sigma_{r+1}(A)^{2}+\ldots+\sigma_{n}(A)^{2}}{n-r}вүӨвҖ–AвҲ’[A]rвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2+Пғr+1вҖӢ(A)2absentsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗҙрқ‘ҹрқ–Ҙ2subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1superscriptрқҗҙ2\displaystyle\leq\|A-[A]_{r}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}+\sigma_{r+1}(A)^{2}which implies вҖ–AвҲ’BвҖ–22вүӨвҖ–AвҲ’[A]rвҖ–22+Пғr+1вҖӢ(A)2=2вҖӢПғr+1вҖӢ(A)2superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗө22superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗҙрқ‘ҹ22subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1superscriptрқҗҙ22subscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹ1superscriptрқҗҙ2\|A-B\|_{2}^{2}\leq\|A-[A]_{r}\|_{2}^{2}+\sigma_{r+1}(A)^{2}=2\sigma_{r+1}(A)^{2}.вҲҺ

Using the above lemma, we have that whenever вҖ–AвҲ’BвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2вүӨ(1+1/n)вҖӢвҖ–AвҲ’[A]1вҖ–рқ–Ҙ2superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗөрқ–Ҙ211рқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗҙ1рқ–Ҙ2\|A-B\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}\leq(1+1/n)\|A-[A]_{1}\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2} for a rank 111 matrix BрқҗөB, then вҖ–AвҲ’BвҖ–22вүӨ2вҖӢвҖ–AвҲ’BвҖ–22superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗө222superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗө22\|A-B\|_{2}^{2}\leq 2\|A-B\|_{2}^{2}. Consider the random matrix рқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} considered in TheoremВ 5.1. With probability вүҘ99/100absent99100\geq 99/100, we have that Пғ1вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙ)/Пғ2вҖӢ(рқ‘ҙ)вүҘ2subscriptрқңҺ1рқ‘ҙsubscriptрқңҺ2рқ‘ҙ2\sigma_{1}(\boldsymbol{M})/\sigma_{2}(\boldsymbol{M})\geq 2 by picking Оұрқӣј\alpha to be a large enough constant.

A tрқ‘Ўt-round randomized algorithm for (1+1/n)11рқ‘ӣ(1+1/n)-approximate rank-111 Frobenius norm LRA thus implies the existence of a (t+1)рқ‘Ў1(t+1) round deterministic algorithm that with probability вүҘ98/100absent98100\geq 98/100 over the random matrix рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} makes general queries such that the squared projection of рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—tensor-productрқ’–рқ’—\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v} onto the query space of the algorithm exceeds n2/64superscriptрқ‘ӣ264n^{2}/64 using similar arguments as in proof of TheoremВ 5.1. Now, using (4), we obtain thattвүҘcвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n)рқ‘Ўрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\displaystyle t\geq c\log(n^{2}/k)/\log\log(n)for a small enough constant cрқ‘җc.вҲҺ

For matrices AрқҗҙA with Пғ1вҖӢ(A)/Пғ2вҖӢ(A)вүҘ2subscriptрқңҺ1рқҗҙsubscriptрқңҺ2рқҗҙ2\sigma_{1}(A)/\sigma_{2}(A)\geq 2, subspace iteration algorithm gives a 1+1/n11рқ‘ӣ1+1/n-approximate solution in OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n))рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣO(\log(n)) rounds using nрқ‘ӣn-linear measurements [10, 20]. The above lower bound shows that if an algorithm is allowed oвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n))рқ‘ңрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣo(\log(n)/\log\log(n)) adaptive rounds, then the algorithm has to make n2вҲ’oвҖӢ(1)superscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ң1n^{2-o(1)} linear measurements in each round, which is almost as many measurements as is required to read the entire matrix.

Given matrices AрқҗҙA, BрқҗөB, and a rank parameter rрқ‘ҹr, the reduced-rank regression problem in spectral norm is defined asminrank-вҖӢrвҖӢXвҒЎвҖ–AвҖӢXвҲ’BвҖ–2.subscriptrank-рқ‘ҹрқ‘Ӣsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқ‘Ӣрқҗө2\displaystyle\min_{\text{rank-}r\ X}\|AX-B\|_{2}.Taking A=IрқҗҙрқҗјA=I, we have that the spectral norm low rank approximation is a special case of the reduced-rank regression problem. Thus we have the following lower bound on the number of rounds of an adaptive algorithm that outputs a 2-approximate solution for the reduced-rank regression problem.

With nвҖӢrрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹnr adaptive linear measurements in each round, the above theorem gives a lower bound of О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n/r)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n))О©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣ\Omega(\log(n/r)/\log\log(n)) on the number of rounds required to obtain a factor 2 approximation. Kacham and Woodruff [15] give an algorithm for reduced-rank regression that outputs constant factor approximations to the reduced-rank problem in OвҖӢ(polyвҒЎ(logвҒЎn))рқ‘Ӯpolyрқ‘ӣO(\operatorname{poly}(\log n)) (ignoring polylogarithmic factors from condition numbers) adaptive rounds using nвҖӢrрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹnr linear measurements in each round.

If the matrix B=M+Pрқҗөрқ‘Җрқ‘ғB=M+P has the structure of a planted matrix studied in this paper with Pрқ‘ғP being a rank rрқ‘ҹr matrix and вҖ–PвҖ–2>10вҖӢвҖ–BвҲ’[B]rвҖ–2subscriptnormрқ‘ғ210subscriptnormрқҗөsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗөрқ‘ҹ2\|P\|_{2}>10\|B-[B]_{r}\|_{2} and if the matrix AрқҗҙA is well conditioned, then we can find an OвҖӢ(1)рқ‘Ӯ1O(1) approximate solution to reduced-rank regression problem in OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n)+logвҒЎ(вҖ–PвҖ–2/OPT))рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣsubscriptnormрқ‘ғ2OPTO(\log(n)+\log(\|P\|_{2}/\text{OPT})) rounds, where OPT is the optimal value of the reduced-rank regression problem.

First, we find a rank rрқ‘ҹr matrix PвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ғвҖІP^{\prime} such that вҖ–BвҲ’PвҖІвҖ–2вүӨ2вҖӢвҖ–BвҲ’[B]rвҖ–2subscriptnormрқҗөsuperscriptрқ‘ғвҖІ22subscriptnormрқҗөsubscriptdelimited-[]рқҗөрқ‘ҹ2\|B-P^{\prime}\|_{2}\leq 2\|B-[B]_{r}\|_{2} in OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n))рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣO(\log(n)) adaptive rounds using the Block Krylov iteration algorithm of [20], which queries nвҖӢrрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹnr linear measurements in each round. Now, for any matrix Xрқ‘ӢX,вҖ–AвҖӢXвҲ’PвҖІвҖ–2=вҖ–AвҖӢXвҲ’BвҖ–2ВұвҖ–BвҲ’PвҖІвҖ–2=вҖ–AвҖӢXвҲ’BвҖ–2Вұ2вӢ…OPT.subscriptnormрқҗҙрқ‘Ӣsuperscriptрқ‘ғвҖІ2plus-or-minussubscriptnormрқҗҙрқ‘Ӣрқҗө2subscriptnormрқҗөsuperscriptрқ‘ғвҖІ2plus-or-minussubscriptnormрқҗҙрқ‘Ӣрқҗө2вӢ…2OPT\displaystyle\|AX-P^{\prime}\|_{2}=\|AX-B\|_{2}\pm\|B-P^{\prime}\|_{2}=\|AX-B\|_{2}\pm 2\cdot\text{OPT}.

Let PвҖІ=UвҖӢОЈвҖӢVрқ–іsuperscriptрқ‘ғвҖІрқ‘ҲОЈsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ–іP^{\prime}=U\Sigma V^{\mathsf{T}} be the singular value decomposition with matrix UвҖӢОЈрқ‘ҲОЈU\Sigma having rрқ‘ҹr columns. Then using high precision regression routines (see [33] and references therein), we find a matrix X~~рқ‘Ӣ\tilde{X} such thatвҖ–AвҖӢX~вҲ’AвҖӢA+вҖӢUвҖӢОЈвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2вүӨОөвҖӢвҖ–UвҖӢОЈвҖ–рқ–Ҙ2вүӨ10вҖӢrвҖӢОөвҖӢвҖ–PвҖ–22.superscriptsubscriptnormрқҗҙ~рқ‘Ӣрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҙрқ‘ҲОЈрқ–Ҙ2рқңҖsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘ҲОЈрқ–Ҙ210рқ‘ҹрқңҖsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘ғ22\displaystyle\|A\tilde{X}-AA^{+}U\Sigma\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}\leq\varepsilon\|U\Sigma\|_{\mathsf{F}}^{2}\leq 10r\varepsilon\|P\|_{2}^{2}.in OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(1/Оө))рқ‘Ӯ1рқңҖO(\log(1/\varepsilon)) iterations, where each iteration queries nвҖӢrрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹnr linear measurements. Again, using the triangle inequality, we haveвҖ–AвҖӢX~вҖӢVрқ–івҲ’PвҖІвҖ–2=вҖ–AвҖӢX~вҲ’UвҖӢОЈвҖ–2вүӨвҖ–AвҖӢA+вҖӢUвҖӢОЈвҲ’AвҖӢX~вҖ–2+вҖ–AвҖӢA+вҖӢUвҖӢОЈвҲ’UвҖӢОЈвҖ–2.subscriptnormрқҗҙ~рқ‘Ӣsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ–іsuperscriptрқ‘ғвҖІ2subscriptnormрқҗҙ~рқ‘Ӣрқ‘ҲОЈ2subscriptnormрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҙрқ‘ҲОЈрқҗҙ~рқ‘Ӣ2subscriptnormрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҙрқ‘ҲОЈрқ‘ҲОЈ2\displaystyle\|A\tilde{X}V^{\mathsf{T}}-P^{\prime}\|_{2}=\|A\tilde{X}-U\Sigma\|_{2}\leq\|AA^{+}U\Sigma-A\tilde{X}\|_{2}+\|AA^{+}U\Sigma-U\Sigma\|_{2}.If XвҲ—superscriptрқ‘ӢX^{*} is the optimal solution for the reduced rank regression problem, we haveвҖ–AвҖӢA+вҖӢUвҖӢОЈвҲ’UвҖӢОЈвҖ–2subscriptnormрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҙрқ‘ҲОЈрқ‘ҲОЈ2\displaystyle\|AA^{+}U\Sigma-U\Sigma\|_{2}=вҖ–AвҖӢA+вҖӢUвҖӢОЈвҖӢVрқ–івҲ’UвҖӢОЈвҖӢVрқ–івҖ–2absentsubscriptnormрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҙрқ‘ҲОЈsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ–ірқ‘ҲОЈsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ–і2\displaystyle=\|AA^{+}U\Sigma V^{\mathsf{T}}-U\Sigma V^{\mathsf{T}}\|_{2}вүӨвҖ–AвҖӢXвҲ—вҲ’PвҖІвҖ–2absentsubscriptnormрқҗҙsuperscriptрқ‘Ӣsuperscriptрқ‘ғвҖІ2\displaystyle\leq\|AX^{*}-P^{\prime}\|_{2}вүӨвҖ–AвҖӢXвҲ—вҲ’BвҖ–2+2вӢ…OPT=3вӢ…OPT.absentsubscriptnormрқҗҙsuperscriptрқ‘Ӣрқҗө2вӢ…2OPTвӢ…3OPT\displaystyle\leq\|AX^{*}-B\|_{2}+2\cdot\text{OPT}=3\cdot\text{OPT}.We also have вҖ–AвҖӢA+вҖӢUвҖӢОЈвҲ’AвҖӢX~вҖ–2вүӨвҖ–AвҖӢA+вҖӢUвҖӢОЈвҲ’AвҖӢX~вҖ–рқ–ҘвүӨOвҖӢ(rвҖӢОөвҖӢвҖ–PвҖ–2)subscriptnormрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҙрқ‘ҲОЈрқҗҙ~рқ‘Ӣ2subscriptnormрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҙрқ‘ҲОЈрқҗҙ~рқ‘Ӣрқ–Ҙрқ‘Ӯрқ‘ҹрқңҖsubscriptnormрқ‘ғ2\|AA^{+}U\Sigma-A\tilde{X}\|_{2}\leq\|AA^{+}U\Sigma-A\tilde{X}\|_{\mathsf{F}}\leq O(\sqrt{r\varepsilon}\|P\|_{2}). We set Оө=(OPT/вҖ–PвҖ–2)2/KвҖӢrрқңҖsuperscriptOPTsubscriptnormрқ‘ғ22рқҗҫрқ‘ҹ\varepsilon=(\text{OPT}/\|P\|_{2})^{2}/Kr for a large enough constant KрқҗҫK and obtain that вҖ–AвҖӢA+вҖӢUвҖӢОЈвҲ’AвҖӢX~вҖ–2вүӨOPTsubscriptnormрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҙрқ‘ҲОЈрқҗҙ~рқ‘Ӣ2OPT\|AA^{+}U\Sigma-A\tilde{X}\|_{2}\leq\text{OPT}. Overall, we have вҖ–AвҖӢX~вҖӢVрқ–івҲ’BвҖ–2вүӨвҖ–AвҖӢX~вҖӢVрқ–івҲ’PвҖІвҖ–2+2вӢ…OPTвүӨ6вӢ…OPTsubscriptnormрқҗҙ~рқ‘Ӣsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ–ірқҗө2subscriptnormрқҗҙ~рқ‘Ӣsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ–іsuperscriptрқ‘ғвҖІ2вӢ…2OPTвӢ…6OPT\|A\tilde{X}V^{\mathsf{T}}-B\|_{2}\leq\|A\tilde{X}V^{\mathsf{T}}-P^{\prime}\|_{2}+2\cdot\text{OPT}\leq 6\cdot\text{OPT}. Thus we obtain a 666-approximate solution in OвҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n)+logвҒЎ(вҖ–PвҖ–2/OPT))рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣsubscriptnormрқ‘ғ2OPTO(\log(n)+\log(\|P\|_{2}/\text{OPT})) iterations given that AрқҗҙA is well-conditioned and BрқҗөB is of the form M+Pрқ‘Җрқ‘ғM+P with вҖ–PвҖ–2вүҘ10вҖӢвҖ–MвҖ–2subscriptnormрқ‘ғ210subscriptnormрқ‘Җ2\|P\|_{2}\geq 10\|M\|_{2} for a rank rрқ‘ҹr matrix Pрқ‘ғP. Thus the lower bound is near optimal for algorithms that output OвҖӢ(1)рқ‘Ӯ1O(1) approximate solution for planted models and well-conditioned coefficient matrices.

Consider the nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n random matrix рқ‘ҙ=рқ‘®+(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘ҙрқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{M}=\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} for a large enough constant Оұрқӣј\alpha. The existence of a tрқ‘Ўt-round algorithm as in the statement implies that there is a deterministic tрқ‘Ўt-round algorithm that outputs approximations to singular vectors of the matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} with probability вүҘ9/10absent910\geq 9/10. We then have that 10вҖӢвҖ–рқ‘®вҖ–2вүӨвҖ–(Оұ/n)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–івҖ–210subscriptnormрқ‘®2subscriptnormрқӣјрқ‘ӣрқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і210\|\boldsymbol{G}\|_{2}\leq\|(\alpha/\sqrt{n})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}}\|_{2} and вҖ–рқ’–вҖ–2,вҖ–рқ’—вҖ–2вүҘn/2subscriptnormрқ’–2subscriptnormрқ’—2рқ‘ӣ2\|\boldsymbol{u}\|_{2},\|\boldsymbol{v}\|_{2}\geq\sqrt{n}/2 with large probability. Suppose v1вҖІsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖІv_{1}^{\prime} is a unit vector such that вҖ–v1вҲ’v1вҖІвҖ–2вүӨ1/10subscriptnormsubscriptрқ‘Ј1superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖІ2110\|v_{1}-v_{1}^{\prime}\|_{2}\leq 1/10. Similarly, |рқ’–рқ–івҖӢu1вҖІ|вүҘ(7/10)superscriptрқ’–рқ–іsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘ў1вҖІ710|\boldsymbol{u}^{\mathsf{T}}u_{1}^{\prime}|\geq(7/10) which impliesвҹЁu1вҖІвҠ—v1вҖІ,рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—вҹ©2=вҹЁu1вҖІ,рқ’–вҹ©2вҖӢвҹЁv1вҖІ,рқ’—вҹ©2вүҘ(49/100)вҖӢвҖ–рқ’–вҖ–22вҖӢвҖ–рқ’—вҖ–22вүҘn2/10.superscripttensor-productsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘ў1вҖІsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖІtensor-productрқ’–рқ’—2superscriptsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘ў1вҖІрқ’–2superscriptsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖІрқ’—249100superscriptsubscriptnormрқ’–22superscriptsubscriptnormрқ’—22superscriptрқ‘ӣ210\displaystyle\langle u_{1}^{\prime}\otimes v_{1}^{\prime},\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v}\rangle^{2}=\langle u_{1}^{\prime},\boldsymbol{u}\rangle^{2}\langle v_{1}^{\prime},\boldsymbol{v}\rangle^{2}\geq(49/100)\|\boldsymbol{u}\|_{2}^{2}\|\boldsymbol{v}\|_{2}^{2}\geq n^{2}/10.Thus, with a large probability over the random matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M}, approximations to the top left and right singular vectors of the matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} can be used to construct an n2superscriptрқ‘ӣ2n^{2}-dimensional unit vector qрқ‘һq such that вҹЁq,рқ’–вҠ—рқ’—вҹ©2вүҘn2/10superscriptрқ‘һtensor-productрқ’–рқ’—2superscriptрқ‘ӣ210\langle q,\boldsymbol{u}\otimes\boldsymbol{v}\rangle^{2}\geq n^{2}/10. Now, (4) implies that t+1вүҘcвҖӢlogвҒЎ(n2/k)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n)рқ‘Ў1рқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣt+1\geq c\log(n^{2}/k)/\log\log(n) for a small enough constant cрқ‘җc.

To extend the above lower bound to approximating iрқ‘–i-th singular vector for all iвүӨn/2рқ‘–рқ‘ӣ2i\leq n/2, we can use the following instance:рқ‘ҙвҖІ=[рқ‘ҙ00S]superscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІmatrixрқ‘ҙ00рқ‘Ҷ\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime}=\begin{bmatrix}\boldsymbol{M}&0\\0&S\end{bmatrix}where рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} is the (n/2)Г—(n/2)рқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ӣ2(n/2)\times(n/2) random matrix рқ‘®+(Оұ/n/2)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјрқ‘ӣ2рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/\sqrt{n/2})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} and Sрқ‘ҶS is a deterministic diagonal matrix chosen such that the top singular vectors of рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} correspond to iрқ‘–i-th singular vectors of the matrix рқ‘ҙвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІ\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime}. If Sрқ‘ҶS is chosen to be the diagonal matrix with iвҲ’1рқ‘–1i-1 values equal to 10вҖӢnвҖӢОұ10рқ‘ӣрқӣј10\sqrt{n}\alpha and the rest of the entries are set to 00, we have that with high probability that the iрқ‘–i-th left and right singular vectors of рқ‘ҙвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ҙвҖІ\boldsymbol{M}^{\prime} correspond to the top left and right singular vectors of рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} as вҖ–MвҖ–2вүӨ10вҖӢnвҖӢОұsubscriptnormрқ‘Җ210рқ‘ӣрқӣј\|M\|_{2}\leq 10\sqrt{n}\alpha with high probability. Now the existence of a tрқ‘Ўt-round randomized algorithm to approximate iрқ‘–i-th left and right singular vectors of an nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n matrix for iвүӨn/2рқ‘–рқ‘ӣ2i\leq n/2 with probability вүҘ9/10absent910\geq 9/10 implies that there is a deterministic tрқ‘Ўt-round algorithm that approximates the top left and right singular vectors of the (n/2)Г—(n/2)рқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ӣ2(n/2)\times(n/2) matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} with probability вүҘ8/10absent810\geq 8/10. From the above argument we have t+1=О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ((n/2)2/k)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n/2))=О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n2/k)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n))рқ‘Ў1О©superscriptрқ‘ӣ22рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ2О©superscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣt+1=\Omega(\log((n/2)^{2}/k)/\log\log(n/2))=\Omega(\log(n^{2}/k)/\log\log(n)).

For iвүҘn/2рқ‘–рқ‘ӣ2i\geq n/2, we can do a similar reduction. We have that the top left singular vector u1subscriptрқ‘ў1u_{1} of the (n/2)Г—(n/2)рқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ӣ2(n/2)\times(n/2) matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} is same as the top singular (eigen-) vector of the matrix рқ‘ҙвҖӢрқ‘ҙрқ–ірқ‘ҙsuperscriptрқ‘ҙрқ–і\boldsymbol{M}\boldsymbol{M}^{\mathsf{T}} and with high probability is equal to the last singular (eigen-) vector of the matrix (100вҖӢnвҖӢОұ2)вҖӢIвҲ’рқ‘ҙвҖӢрқ‘ҙрқ–і100рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқӣј2рқҗјрқ‘ҙsuperscriptрқ‘ҙрқ–і(100n\alpha^{2})I-\boldsymbol{M}\boldsymbol{M}^{\mathsf{T}}. Using the same trick as above, we can create an nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n matrix such that the iрқ‘–i-th singular vector for iвүҘn/2рқ‘–рқ‘ӣ2i\geq n/2 corresponds to u1subscriptрқ‘ў1u_{1}. Instead of рқ‘ҙвҖӢрқ‘ҙрқ–ірқ‘ҙsuperscriptрқ‘ҙрқ–і\boldsymbol{M}\boldsymbol{M}^{\mathsf{T}}, if we use the matrix рқ‘ҙрқ–івҖӢрқ‘ҙsuperscriptрқ‘ҙрқ–ірқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M}^{\mathsf{T}}\boldsymbol{M}, then we can make the top right singular vector v1subscriptрқ‘Ј1v_{1} of the matrix рқ‘ҙрқ‘ҙ\boldsymbol{M} correspond to the iрқ‘–i-th singular vector of an nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n matrix. Thus, for all iвҲҲ[n]рқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘ӣi\in[n], we have an О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ(n2/k)/logвҒЎlogвҒЎ(n))О©superscriptрқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\Omega(\log(n^{2}/k)/\log\log(n)) lower bound for any randomized algorithm that computes the iрқ‘–i-th left and right singular vectors of an arbitrary nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n matrix AрқҗҙA using kрқ‘ҳk linear measurements of AрқҗҙA in each round of the algorithm.

The lower bounds for algorithms that output approximations to singular vectors with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/polyвҒЎ(n)absent11polyрқ‘ӣ\geq 1-1/\operatorname{poly}(n) follow similarly using the high probability lower bounds from (5).вҲҺ

The following theorem gives a lower bound of О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ(m/k))О©рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳ\Omega(\log(m/k)) rounds on adaptive algorithms that compute 222-approximate spectral norm LRA for matrices with at most mрқ‘ҡm nonzero entries.

We consider the distribution of the mГ—mрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҡ\sqrt{m}\times\sqrt{m} random matrix рқ‘®+(Оұ/m1/4)вҖӢрқ’–вҖӢрқ’—рқ–ірқ‘®рқӣјsuperscriptрқ‘ҡ14рқ’–superscriptрқ’—рқ–і\boldsymbol{G}+(\alpha/m^{1/4})\boldsymbol{u}\boldsymbol{v}^{\mathsf{T}} for a large enough constant Оұрқӣј\alpha and embed this instance into an nГ—nрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\times n matrix. Clearly, all the matrices drawn from this distribution have at most mрқ‘ҡm nonzero entries. And from TheoremВ 5.3, any deterministic algorithm using kрқ‘ҳk linear measurements in each round and computing a 222-approximate spectral norm approximation for a matrix drawn from this distribution, with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/polyвҒЎ(m)absent11polyрқ‘ҡ\geq 1-1/\operatorname{poly}(m), must use О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ((m)2/k))=О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ(m/k))О©superscriptрқ‘ҡ2рқ‘ҳО©рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳ\Omega(\log((\sqrt{m})^{2}/k))=\Omega(\log(m/k)) rounds.

Thus by YaoвҖҷs minimax lemma, any randomized algorithm that outputs a 222-approximate spectral norm approximation with probability вүҘ1вҲ’1/polyвҒЎ(m)absent11polyрқ‘ҡ\geq 1-1/\operatorname{poly}(m) for an arbitrary matrix with mрқ‘ҡm nonzero entries must use t=О©вҖӢ(logвҒЎ(m/k))рқ‘ЎО©рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳt=\Omega(\log(m/k)) rounds.вҲҺ

The above theorem implies that any algorithm with only OвҖӢ(1)рқ‘Ӯ1O(1) adaptive rounds must query О©вҖӢ(m)О©рқ‘ҡ\Omega(m) linear measurements. This lower bound is tight up to constant factors as with 2вҖӢm2рқ‘ҡ2m linear measurements, since all of the mрқ‘ҡm non-zero entries of any arbitrary matrix can be computed in just 111 round using a Vandermonde matrix [8, TheoremВ 2.14].
